Current Commentary

Japan's Issue of Discipline and the Saito Cabinet 26

Since the assassination of Inukai Tsuyoshi and the rise of Saito Makoto, Japanese parliamentary politics has shown its decline, while the power of the military has surged uncontrollably. However, since the outbreak of the "September 18th" Incident, Japan's domestic economic panic has become increasingly acute, and the rural problem has become even more serious. Politicians generally believe that this is a good opportunity to attack the military in order to maintain their lives. Therefore, they first exposed the so-called issue of military discipline to embarrass the military clique, and then exposed the bribery scandal of the Minister of Education to lay the groundwork for the downfall of the cabinet.

The evidence for the bribery scandal of the Minister of Education, Hatoyama Ichiro, exposed by Okamoto Ichiki, a member of the Seiyukai, is recorded in the prosecutor's office, which is by no means comparable to unfounded rumors. It reminds people of the fact that the Japanese education sector is impoverished. The teachers' salaries are in arrears, making it difficult for them to make a living. Therefore, various temptations have taken advantage of the opportunity to advance. The scandal of bribery in the education sector, from elementary schools to the highest institutions of learning such as Nagasaki Medical University, has long been spread throughout the country. Now, even the highest educational administrative leader is colluding in this. The reflection of the so-called issue of discipline is truly noteworthy. Moreover, since the occurrence of the Tatsukawa Professor Incident, the freedom to conduct academic research in Japan has become mere empty talk. However, the repercussions have not only affected ordinary teachers and students in the lower classes, who are willing to be infected by the deterioration, but even the children of the Gakushuin, who have received aristocratic education, cannot avoid leaning to the left. From this, it can be inferred that the entire Japanese society is filled with corruption and deterioration. The issue of discipline caused by Hatoyama's bribery is only one aspect of it.

However, whether the uproar of the issue of discipline caused by the exposure by a member of parliament is a sign of the resurgence of parliamentary politics is still doubtful. The fact that all major political parties in Japan rely on the support of special financial groups, such as the Seiyukai's reliance on the Mitsui financial group and the Minseito's reliance on the Mitsubishi financial group, has long been an open secret. The fact that the South Manchurian Railway is the financial source for the ruling party is also well known and cannot be deeply denied. Therefore, it is self-inflicted to cause resentment among the people and encounter attacks from the military. Since the outbreak of the September 18th Incident, the clumsy policies of the military have taken the opportunity to rise. The shortcomings of Japanese parliamentary politics have been completely exposed, and the shortcomings of military politics cannot be compensated. The weak Saito cabinet has been able to maintain the life of its so-called transcendent cabinet due to the mutual restraint between the military and political parties. On the one hand, it claims to be leading through extraordinary times and introducing constitutional normalcy. On the other hand, it is still inevitably subject to the control of the military. Logically speaking, it is not easy for the current cabinet, as a mixed cabinet that transcends political parties and wavers between the two major parties, to carry out the so-called affairs of an extraordinary time. For the military, it is only borrowing it to perfunctorily maintain the facade of constitutional politics and continue to promote military policies.

Now that the issue of discipline has broken out, the future of the cabinet is in serious crisis. It is doubtful whether Saito, who is currently claiming illness, can continue to hold office. However, even if the Saito cabinet collapses, Suzuki or Wakatsuki are unlikely to form a cabinet alone. Since the parliament is not easy to control and the relationship with the military is even more difficult to fulfill satisfactorily, the restoration of the so-called constitutional norm is likely to become a fantasy. In the future, regardless of whether Kazuhiko Yada, Fumimaro Konoe, or Korekiyo Takahashi and others are appointed to form a cabinet, they will inevitably flaunt the beautiful name of national unity and rely on the whims of the army and navy. This can be asserted.

Shocking!! Will Germany Recognize the Puppet Manchukuo? 27

Losing Trade in China

Further Undermining the League of Nations' Stance

American Media Believe Germany Wouldn't Be So Unwise

Washington is Considering How to Respond

(New York) A reporter stationed in Tokyo for the "Guidance Report," when discussing the possibility of Germany recognizing "Manchukuo," stated that if Germany recognized "Manchukuo," it would inevitably lose a portion of its trade with China. Therefore, Germany must first consider whether the future trade it gains from "Manchukuo" can compensate for its losses. At the same time, it must consider whether it is unwise to further strike the League of Nations by undermining the League's decision not to recognize "Manchukuo," a decision in whose passage Germany itself had participated. (TASS dispatch, 21st)

(Washington) Only eight days after Puyi changed his title to "Emperor of Manchukuo" and ascended the throne, government officials and the national press here are once again paying close attention to the issue of recognizing "Manchukuo." President Roosevelt stated today during a meeting with reporters that the matter is quite complex and he is unwilling to make any pronouncements until he has consulted with the Secretary of State. Recently, some have argued that the United States, having joined hands with Russia, should immediately recognize "Manchukuo" so that American trade in "Manchukuo" can increase. However, most people suspect that if the United States recognizes "Manchukuo," American trade with China will be greatly affected. The New York Daily News is even actively promoting the idea that recognizing "Manchukuo" would be sufficient to develop American commerce. However, according to important figures in Washington, they do not believe there is any possibility of recognizing "Manchukuo," and the matter of Puyi's ascension to the throne is completely unrelated to the United States. (National News Agency dispatch, 21st)

(Washington) According to reliable sources, Japan seems to intend to make American recognition of "Manchukuo" a prerequisite for Japan's participation in the 1935 naval conference. However, as of now, Japan has not yet made this request, because "Manchukuo" is currently unable to protect American citizens from bandit attacks. If the United States were to recognize it, it would actually put "Manchukuo" in a difficult position. However, American officials are quite concerned about Japan's intentions. Once the effective term of the London Naval Treaty is about to expire, will the United States ultimately decide to strictly adhere to the principle of non-recognition of "Manchukuo" announced by former Secretary of State Stimson, or will it engage in another arms race in the Pacific? Which of these two options will the United States abandon? At that time, it may be inevitable that there will be some wavering. It is rumored that certain European countries will recognize "Manchukuo" imminently. Diplomatic circles believe that Germany may take this action, because after Germany recognizes it, both sides will benefit economically. Manchuria exports 3 million tons of soybeans annually, of which 1 million tons are shipped to Germany. Last year, Germany imposed a heavy import tax on soybeans, which greatly affected Manchurian soybeans. Its inventory has reached 2 million tons. If Germany recognizes "Manchukuo," it will definitely sign a commercial treaty with it, and in the future, "Manchukuo" will export soybeans to Germany and use the proceeds to purchase German goods, benefiting both sides. (Havas dispatch, 21st)

(Washington) People here have heard rumors that certain European countries will soon recognize "Manchukuo" and are eager to understand what attitude the United States will take if such a situation occurs. Judging from the news coming out of the White House today, the United States will naturally consider such a situation if it develops, but the doctrine announced by former Secretary of State Stimson, namely not recognizing countries created by force or aggression, may not be implemented mechanically. (Note: On January 7, 1932, the United States sent notes to China and Japan stating that the United States could not recognize Japan's occupation of Manchuria as legal, and that the system established after the occupation, because it violated the Open Door Policy and the Nine-Power Treaty, could not be recognized. On February 24 of the same year, Stimson reiterated the need to maintain China's Open Door Policy in his letter to Senator Borah and recognized the necessity of maintaining the Washington Nine-Power Treaty.) (Havas dispatch, 21st)

Rumor Has It The US Will Change Far East Policy 28

A Trend Towards Adopting A More Moderate Attitude Towards Japan

Abandoning Military Bases In The Philippine Islands

The Stimson Doctrine Is Not Intended To Be Maintained

(Washington) The new plan of the US authorities is to abandon the US naval and military bases in the Philippine Islands in order to obtain the acceptance of the Philippine Islands' independence plan. (Reuters dispatch, 22nd)

(New York) The New York newspaper's Washington dispatch stated that the United States has a tendency to adopt a moderate attitude towards the issue of recognizing "Manchukuo." If the League of Nations changes its policy, the United States may abandon the doctrine proclaimed by Stimson that the United States does not recognize territorial changes created by force. (Reuters dispatch, 22nd)

The Atmosphere in the Japanese Upper House Deteriorates Sharply, a Vigorous Movement to Overthrow the Cabinet 29

Takahashi Serves as Acting Prime Minister

Seeking Parliamentary Approval

The Seiyukai Advocates a Grand Coalition of Political Parties

Councilor Sunada Vigorously Criticizes the Government for Incompetence

(Tokyo) The Budget Committee of the Upper House, due to Prime Minister Saito and Agriculture Minister Goto being ill and other cabinet members unable to attend, has made no progress in deliberations. Of the 24 people who had notified that they would ask questions, only four have completed their questioning. For example, Count Katsuta only reserved his questions for Prime Minister Saito, and others withdrew their questions. As a result, some advocated extending the budget deliberation period, but there were also considerable objections. However, the atmosphere in the Upper House is showing signs of deterioration due to the sluggish state of Prime Minister Saito and others, and the entire atmosphere is moving towards a movement to overthrow the cabinet. (Dentsu dispatch, 22nd)

(Tokyo) Due to Prime Minister Saito's inability to attend the Upper House, the budget general meeting is planning to extend the session to the 25th. According to the doctor, the Prime Minister will have difficulty attending the session even on the 26th. In order to resolve the budget proposal, the Japanese government plans to decide on a temporary prime minister at tomorrow's cabinet meeting. It is heard that Finance Minister Takahashi will assume this position to deal with the Diet. (United Chinese Press dispatch, 22nd)

(Tokyo) This morning, due to Prime Minister Saito's illness and inability to attend the Diet, the Upper House requested the government to appoint a temporary acting prime minister who would only be responsible for answering questions in the Diet without any legal basis. After Secretary-General Horikiri reported this to Prime Minister Saito and obtained the Prime Minister's consent, he visited Finance Minister Takahashi and Interior Minister Yamata. The two ministers consulted at 11 a.m. this morning and decided to accept the Upper House's proposal and appoint Finance Minister Takahashi to serve in this position. In the afternoon, Secretary-General Horikiri met with various factions of the Upper House, reported the government's decision, and requested formal recognition of Finance Minister Takahashi's appointment as temporary acting prime minister. (United Chinese Press dispatch, 22nd)

(Tokyo) Fifty-two members of the Seiyukai's Grand Coalition faction, including Azuma and Kinoshita, held a meeting last night at the Shiba San'entei to deliberate on the methods for promoting the party's unification movement. They resolved that in order to overcome the difficult situation, they must seek sincere unity. To unite the various political parties, they should start with self-awareness. Based on the Japanese ideology of "one sovereign and ten thousand people" and the spirit of the party, they want to seek the grand unity of the party. With this policy, they selected executive committee members to visit various factions and seek their participation. By this morning, 64 people from various factions had already joined. With these 84 people as initiators, they issued invitations to Diet members from various factions, seeking their participation, and scheduled a general meeting for the 25th. Although this movement is called a "grand coalition," it is actually not very beneficial to the Suzuki faction. (United Chinese Press dispatch, 22nd)

(Tokyo) Today's plenary session of the House of Representatives was declared open by Speaker Akita at 1:25 p.m. After reporting on various bills, Mr. Sunada Shigemasa of the Seiyukai took the stage to speak on the matter of proceeding with the agenda, declaring:

The session is now more than halfway over, but important bills have not yet been submitted. The Prime Minister and the Agriculture Minister claim to be ill and have not been seen attending the Diet. In this situation, what is the point? We have no choice but to conclude that the government lacks enthusiasm for deliberating on important cases. From this perspective, there is a need for an acting minister to handle affairs. No proposals have yet been found for rural relief bills. What is the reason? Now, although we hear that the National Alliance will submit a motion of no confidence, the government should make clear whether it intends to submit important proposals related to the lives of the people. If we know that the government is incompetent, after confirming it, we should resolutely submit a motion of no confidence. Before today's meeting is adjourned, we should ask the responsible government officials to give a clear answer.

Speaker Akita declared,

The gist of Mr. Sunada's speech is to warn the government. Now that the three ministers of the army, navy, and iron are present, they may be able to represent the government and provide an explanation, or it is not impossible.

Minister Sanshi Tetsu replied that he would now represent the government and answer:

The Prime Minister has already stated at the budget general meeting that various proposals and additional budgets for rural countermeasures are now being devised to be submitted as soon as possible. This has been delayed due to the illness of Agriculture Minister Goto, but it can be decided and seconded recently.

Next, Ms. Toda Yumi of the National Alliance raised a question: Why has the speaker not earnestly deliberated on the motion of no confidence submitted by the National Alliance? Why do the Seiyukai and the Minseito want to prevent the deliberation of the motion of no confidence and adopt such a despicable attitude?

Ms. Toda criticized the contradictions of the Seimin parties and desperately called for support for the deliberation of the motion of no confidence.

Speaker Akita replied:

The motion of no confidence submitted by the National Alliance has already been listed on the agenda, but it has not yet come up in the rotation.

The Diet members of the National Alliance then advocated submitting an urgent motion to change the agenda, but it was rejected due to a minority. The Diet members of the Seimin parties then stormed out of the Diet. After that, they discussed the Export Law Amendment Bill (Trade Control Law) and other laws, which were all entrusted to committees separately. (United Press dispatch, 22nd)

(Tokyo) The investigation committee on the Okamoto Kazumi case has been opened three times. The illegal activities of Minister of Education Hatoyama and other political party members have been gradually revealed. The Diet members of the National Alliance and the First Control Office, with the support of nationalist groups such as the Kodo Society, the Meirin Society, and the Kokuhonsha, will do their utmost to expose the crimes of political party members, and will also reveal incidents such as the Seiyukai elder Teijiro Yamamoto receiving a bribe of 50,000 yen and former Prime Minister Hamaguchi Yuko receiving a bribe of 100,000 yen, thereby arousing public resentment against political parties. The Seiyukai and the Minseito, having learned of this news, are very concerned and have decided to find a way to prevent the situation from escalating. After the investigation committee reopens once or twice, they will decide to end it with the majority force of the Seimin parties in order to prevent Okamoto from taking the opportunity to expose various crimes as much as possible, and have also decided to punish Okamoto for the crime of intentionally harming the reputation of others through his speech, in accordance with the Diet Law. (United Chinese Press dispatch, 22nd)

Countries Excluding Japanese Goods, Japan Planning Countermeasures 30

(Tokyo) In order to properly handle the international economic war, the three ministries of Finance, Commerce and Industry, and Foreign Affairs are studying legislation related to trade and commerce. A general consensus has already been reached. The Commerce Deliberation Council will be held at the Ministry of Foreign Affairs on the 23rd to determine the government's final policy, which is scheduled to be submitted to the Diet next week. The content of the bill is quite simple, namely, if foreign countries set high tariffs or prevent imports, or take any unfriendly measures against Japanese commerce, the government may take appropriate measures as necessary. The authority is extremely inclusive and broad, giving the government dictatorial power over trade countermeasures to deal with the pressure from various countries. (Dentsu dispatch, 22nd)

Anglo-Japanese Cotton Industry Talks on the Verge of Collapse 31

The British Persist in Not Yielding to Japan

The Meeting Next Wednesday is Worth Watching

(Tokyo) According to a dispatch from London, the official meeting of the Anglo-Japanese spinning industry opened at 10:30 a.m. on the 20th and discussed for three and a half hours. However, due to the issue of geographical scope, no results were obtained, and negotiations were extended to the 28th. It is heard that at that day's meeting, representatives from both the British and Japanese sides insisted on their own claims and did not concede. Representatives from both sides had heated discussions on the geographical scope issue of the memorandum of understanding from the British Barrow representative, but no consensus was reached, and the negotiations were completely blocked. As a result of the Japanese delegation's deliberations on the 21st, they believed that the British side's attitude was tough and there was no other way for the meeting to end except in a breakdown. Therefore, the meeting was reopened from 6:30 p.m. and, after coordinating the aftermath, it was decided to telegraph the Osaka General Assembly to ask for instructions on what attitude should be taken if the British side still does not concede on the 28th. It is heard that the British side will also hold a meeting on the 26th to decide on its final attitude. However, the British side has no intention of changing its attitude, so it is generally expected that the Anglo-Japanese talks will take the meeting on the 28th as the final meeting. However, what attitude the two governments will take before the meeting breaks down is worth watching. (United News dispatch, 22nd)

Hirota Reports on Diplomacy with Russia in the Lower House 32

Efforts to Negotiate with Russia over Fishing Zone Disputes

The Key Issue in East Road Negotiations is the Exchange Rate

(Tokyo) Foreign Minister Hirota requested to speak at today's plenary session of the House of Representatives, stating the following:

Now that I hear that the plenary session of the House of Representatives is temporarily adjourned, I would like to report on the recent relations with the Soviet Union while the session is open. Regarding the issue of fishing zone bidding in Vladivostok on the 20th of this month, the government has been conducting various negotiations. The Soviet ambassador visited today and applied to correct the results of the previous bidding. This matter is expected to be resolved. As for the negotiations between Manchukuo and the Soviet Union on the East Road, they had stalled due to differences in the ruble exchange rate. Recently, the opinions of both sides have gradually converged on the issue of the exchange rate. I feel that there has been a turning point in these negotiations. In short, the policy towards the Soviet Union that I have adopted is to try to resolve the pending issues between the two countries separately, one by one. Under this policy, we will continue to work hard in the future. (United News dispatch, 22nd)

(Tokyo) At the time of the Russian-controlled fishing zone bidding, the Japanese bid was declared invalid. The Japanese Ministry of Foreign Affairs yesterday afternoon telegraphed Ambassador Ota in Russia, instructing him to negotiate with the Soviet Union, saying that the Soviet government's unilateral change of the ruble exchange rate was illegal and that the declaration of invalidity of the Japanese bid must be cancelled. At the same time, pending the report of Consul General Watanabe in Vladivostok, the fishing zones that the Japanese side should obtain will be negotiated again. According to Ambassador Ota's report, Counselor Sakako visited the acting director of the Far East Department of the Soviet government on the morning of the 20th and strongly protested about the fishing zone issue. The acting director of the Far East Department replied that the change in the ruble exchange rate must be coordinated by the Japanese and Soviet governments, and that this view was reasonable. The Soviet government will carefully study the matter and decide on countermeasures. Although the fishing zone bidding in Vladivostok was conducted by other official agencies, the central government will also consider solutions. Counselor Sakako also asked whether it was possible to telegraph local official agencies not to force Japan to change the ruble exchange rate. The acting director replied that he would wait for the report from Vladivostok. The results of the negotiations on that day were as such, and it can be seen that the Soviet government also recognizes the legitimacy of the Japanese claims. There is a glimmer of hope in this morning's negotiations. (Dentsu News Agency dispatch, 22nd)

(Tokyo) On the issue of the Russo-Japanese zone dispute, the number of people in both the government and the public in Japan who advocate taking this opportunity to revise the 1931 agreement is increasing day by day. It is said that during the negotiations in 1931 on the ruble exchange rate, the Russian side initially proposed that one ruble was worth 50 Japanese sen in gold, but after many twists and turns, it was finally set at 32.5 sen. Calculated at 32.5 sen, the fishing zone rental fee would also be more than 2 million yen. If it is changed to 75 sen, the rental fee would double to more than 4 million yen. The cost is too high, and it is inconvenient to take a dumping policy abroad, which is a matter of survival for the Japanese North Pacific fishing industry. There are two noteworthy points in the Russian side's strategy this time: one is that the Russian side helps various commercial countries to bid for the fishing zones at the highest price, and the other is that it changes the currency exchange rate, so that the Japanese side increases the burden and increases the cost, making it impossible to compete with Russian canned goods. The Russian side has used these legal means to make the Japanese side abandon the North Pacific fishing zone, which can be said to be a crisis for the Japanese fishing industry. Japanese officials and businessmen want to use this excuse to demand that Russia revise the treaty, which expires in 1936. It is difficult to predict whether the Russian side will allow the Japanese side's request before the expiration. (United Chinese Press dispatch, 22nd)

Italy, Austria, and Hungary are Proceeding with an Economic Alliance 33

The Italian Undersecretary is Warmly Welcomed Upon Arriving in Budapest

Mussolini Looming as the Leader of the Alliance

The Little Entente Countries are Deeply Wary

Budapest When Italian Undersecretary of Foreign Affairs Suvich arrived here today, both the station and nearby buildings were adorned with the national flags of Italy and Hungary to express their welcome. Suvich gave a speech in Győr, in which he expressed his extreme happiness at his arrival, "but if my footsteps today were to fall on the undivided territory of Greater Hungary, then my joy would be even greater."

Italian Undersecretary Suvich met with Prime Minister Gömbös and Foreign Minister Kánya this evening, and then the Hungarian government invited Suvich to dinner. During the dinner, Gömbös gave a welcoming speech, saying that Hungary had a very good feeling for Italy and Italian Prime Minister Mussolini, and that the Italian Prime Minister's friendship towards Hungary was especially appreciated by the Hungarian people. Suvich replied that the Italian Prime Minister deeply understood the situation in Hungary, and the complexity and seriousness of the current international situation proved that the two countries had a close cooperation to seek economic and political restoration to normalcy. Suvich continued, "Italy is currently studying various major issues in order to achieve the peaceful transformation of the Danube region and Europe. The friendship between Italy and Hungary is a major factor in Italy's policy." (Havas dispatch, 21st)

(Paris) The "Le Petit Parisien" commented on the visit of Italian Foreign Minister Suvich to Hungary, saying that Suvich's trip was not only to plan a meeting between the prime ministers of Italy, Austria, and Hungary, but also to lay the foundation for an economic combination of Italy, Austria, and Hungary, and that Italy would guide it. This is not just the opinion of "Le Petit Parisien." The French press all hold this view. "Le Petit Parisien" also said that some say that this attempt is to help Austria so that Germany does not threaten its independence and economic resources, but Romania, Czechoslovakia, and Yugoslavia cannot but be wary when they hear of this plan. The newspaper also said, "Any movement to revise treaties and encourage Hungary to move in this direction, even if its intention is to free Hungary from Germany's restraint, Romania, Czechoslovakia, and Yugoslavia will inevitably view this action with concern. Therefore, the only rational path is still the policy indicated by Czech Foreign Minister Beneš, that is, to find ways for the small countries of Central Europe and the Balkans to cooperate economically. This kind of cooperation can be approved by major powers, but cannot be interfered with by them." (Havas dispatch, 22nd)

Budapest Today, when Italian Undersecretary of Foreign Affairs Suvich arrived here, the newspapers in the Hungarian capital all expressed a warm welcome. For example, the government organ "Pesti Hírlap" stated that Italy and Hungary's peaceful policies are essentially one and the same, that these peaceful policies aim to reform the environment, but take a purely peaceful path, and that Suvich's visit here can be considered a part of this peaceful policy, because it can quickly resolve issues related to the Danube region. Furthermore, Austria has now cleared out the Socialist Party and is carrying out internal construction. Naturally, it does not want to join the negotiations between Italy and Hungary. The nationalist newspaper "Magyarság" stated that the close cooperation between Austria and Hungary for fourteen years has been unable to be realized due to the restrictions of the Little Entente, and that the restoration of the Danube region has become a pie in the sky. Now, only one person and only one country can re-establish the Danube region on bedrock. This one person and this one country is Mussolini and Italy. The liberal newspaper "Pesti Napló" said that Hungary has benefited a lot from Italy in the past, but Italy will never be disappointed. Now, the facts prove that this is not false, because Hungary is now devoted to Fascism and is not a follower of the Nordic ideal. (National News Agency dispatch, 20th)

Anglo-German Talks End 34

Exchange of Views on Disarmament, Good Impression

Lord Eden Leaves Berlin for Rome

(Berlin) British Envoy Lord Eden, accompanied by British Ambassador to Germany, Sir Eric Phipps, visited German Foreign Minister Neurath this morning to continue yesterday's negotiations, which have now come to an end. (National News dispatch, 22nd)

(Berlin) Today, German Chancellor Hitler, Foreign Minister Neurath, and Propaganda Minister Goebbels were invited by British Ambassador Sir Eric Phipps and Lord Privy Seal Eden to lunch at the British Embassy. This was actually the first time Hitler had accepted an invitation as a guest to dine at a foreign embassy. After lunch, Hitler and the others stayed at the embassy and talked with Phipps and Eden for more than two hours. However, the actual exchange of views was conducted by the German Chancellor and the British disarmament expert. It is said that the British envoy's stay in Berlin this time was not for any "negotiations," but only to gather the latest views from all aspects of Germany related to Britain's recent disarmament memorandum in order to study whether any reconciliation methods can be established between Britain and Germany to reduce the causes of differences of opinion. Judging from the length of time that Hitler and Eden spent studying each other today and yesterday, and the good spirits of both sides after the meeting, it can be seen that both sides must have felt extremely satisfied with this conversation. The good impression that Hitler and Eden gave each other has become even more enhanced today, because both of them had served on the front lines in the European War, and they had a lot of fun mentioning the past during this meeting. Tonight, Eden did not issue any news, and the news released by the German Ministry of Foreign Affairs only stated that the talks were still continuing today and could be concluded approximately by tomorrow. Eden's stay here will be extended for 24 hours, and he will leave here for Italy on Friday. (National News dispatch, 21st)

Major Debate in the British House of Commons on the Austro-German Question 35

The Labor Party is Dissatisfied with the Current Situation in Austria

Expresses Dissent to the Three-Power Declaration

(London) The House of Commons reopened the debate on the Austrian question. Labor Party Member of Parliament Wedgwood questioned why the governments of the three countries (Britain, France, and Italy) jointly issued a declaration protecting Austria's independence, saying that the current Austrian government's punishment of socialists was inhumane, and asked whether the British government had stated that it would not protect such a government, even if it did not cost a single blow. Foreign Secretary Simon immediately read out the original text of the Three-Power Declaration and said that this declaration was only announcing principles, and although it stated that Austria's independence needed to be maintained, it was limited to "according to the current treaty." Wedgwood also asked whether Britain could not make the Austrian government's prior restoration of democracy a condition for guaranteeing Austria's independence. The Foreign Secretary was unwilling to answer this question. Subsequently, other Labor Party members of parliament successively protested against Austrian Prime Minister Dollfuss's domestic policy. The views of the British trade unionists on the current situation in Austria can be glimpsed from the speeches made by the parliamentarians. Some people also asked what decision Britain would make regarding Austria's plan to appeal directly to the League of Nations. Foreign Secretary Simon reiterated that, legally speaking, a government could not unilaterally make a decision on behalf of the League of Nations. Wedgwood also asked whether the British government had advised the Austrian government to be lenient, but the Austrian government recently took punitive actions, seemingly disregarding British advice, and whether the British attitude would be affected by this matter. Simon refused to answer this question. Finally, several Labor Party members of parliament said that Austria was becoming a pan-Germanic country and that workers did not have the right to organize. Such a country should not be given aid. (Havas dispatch, 21st)

Cuban Military Officers' Anti-Government Plot Discovered 36

Havana The new Cuban government had been in power for just over a month when it was almost overthrown today. Several army officers plotted to carry out a violent coup, which was fortunately discovered by the authorities and stopped with strict measures. A Chilly Morning Breeze, Thick Fog Envelops 37

Belgian King's Funeral Held

The Procession Stretched Three Miles, Solemn and Reverent

Dignitaries from Various Nations Attended, Including the President of France as a Pallbearer

New King to Be Crowned Today; Republicans Will Seize the Opportunity to Demonstrate

Brussels – This morning, at dawn, a chilly breeze blew, and thick fog enveloped the city. Thousands of veterans slowly walked past the remains of the Belgian King, expressing their final respects to their late sovereign. The King's coffin, draped in the national flag and placed on a gun carriage, rested on the driveway of the Royal Palace. Although it was still early, mourners had already gathered in droves, as if the entire nation had come to pay their respects. Among the veterans were disabled soldiers. After they had marched past in formation, troops from the Allied Powers of the war followed. Then, the gun carriage moved, and the pallbearers reverently proceeded at a slow pace. At this time, the bells of the churches and the cannons of the military paid tribute in mourning. Apart from this, the city was as silent as a tomb. The gun carriage bearing the King's coffin slowly advanced through the troops. The Crown Prince and others closely followed behind. Then came dignitaries such as French President Lebrun, the British Crown Prince, the King of Bulgaria, the Queen of the Netherlands' consort, and the Danish Crown Prince. From the Royal Palace to the Saint Gudule Cathedral, the procession stretched three miles. Crowds of people lined both sides of the route, with every inch of space occupied. Windows, balconies, and even rooftops were packed. When the hearse arrived at the Saint Gudule Cathedral, its bells tolled solemnly. Military flags were arrayed at the entrance, and priests escorted the coffin into the church. The funeral service then began at 11:15 AM. The church was dimly lit, and the black curtains that were hung low added to the somber atmosphere. Soon after, the King's coffin was placed on the altar, with his ceremonial robes, helmet, and sword displayed beside it. Once everything was in place, the black round curtain was removed from above, and incense smoke filled the air, emanating from the censers suspended above the coffin. The Duke and Duchess of Brabant sat behind to the left and right. Archbishop Marie-Léonce conducted the solemn requiem mass and read the absolution. The crowds outside the church stood silently with their hats removed, listening to the service. After the service, the coffin was placed back on the hearse and transported through the heart of the city to the Church of Our Lady for the final benediction. Finally, the coffin was carried to the Royal Crypt at Laeken, where it was laid to rest amidst a 21-gun salute. (Reuter, 22nd)

Brussels – Today, as preparations for the Belgian King's funeral are nearing completion, rumors have suddenly spread that radical supporters of establishing a republic may stage a demonstration tomorrow when the Crown Prince is sworn in to succeed the throne. The authorities are now working hard to prevent any unforeseen events during the King's funeral and the new King's accession. The police are making every effort to protect the dignitaries from various countries who have come to attend the funeral and inauguration. Those who will be escorting the Belgian King's coffin to the Royal Crypt at Laeken include the King of Bulgaria, the King of Siam, the British Crown Prince, the Italian Crown Prince, the Norwegian Crown Prince, the Swedish Crown Prince, the Danish Crown Prince, and the Romanian Crown Prince. Across major European cities, mourning will be uniformly observed for the Belgian King's funeral. The British King and Queen will attend the memorial service at Westminster Abbey in London and the funeral service at Saint Gudule Cathedral in Brussels. At the same time, a service will also be held at St. Paul's Cathedral in London. The British Broadcasting Corporation will broadcast the service from Saint Gudule Cathedral at 11:00 AM this morning (Greenwich Mean Time, which is 7:00 PM Shanghai time). A British delegation is attending the funeral. The British Crown Prince arrived in Brussels yesterday on his private plane, escorted from Lympne by a squadron of Royal Air Force aircraft to the Belgian coast. Upon arriving in Brussels, he was welcomed at the airfield by Prince Charles, the second son of the Belgian King. Admiral Keyes, Commander-in-Chief of the British Fleet, and Viscount Alanbrooke arrived in Zeebrugge yesterday afternoon aboard the cruiser HMS Caradoc, escorted by the destroyer HMS Winchester. The ships carried fifty sailors and members of the Royal Marines band. The entire group traveled to Brussels by special train. The Royal Air Force has also dispatched seven officers and a hundred other ranks, along with the Fifth Dragoon Guards band, to attend the funeral. Representatives from many countries in Europe and beyond are participating. Simultaneously, the heads of state of ten countries around the world are either attending in person or sending representatives. When the doors of the Royal Palace were closed after the tributes concluded, thousands of citizens still stood reverently outside, hoping for a chance to pay their respects. The only conflict that occurred yesterday was when Flemish nationalist members of parliament walked out of the parliamentary hall when an official praised the Belgian King's achievements. They have now decided not to attend the Crown Prince's swearing-in ceremony tomorrow, because the oath is purely a Belgian affair, and the Prime Minister should not have praised the late Belgian King in the assembly using only French. (Reuter, 22nd)

(Tokyo) – The grand funeral of Belgian King Albert I is scheduled to take place in Brussels on the 22nd. On the same day, the Belgian Embassy in Tokyo will hold a solemn memorial service at a Catholic church at 11:00 AM.

The Emperor and Empress of Japan will be represented at the ceremony by Prince Chichibu and his consort. Foreign Minister Hirota, the Army Minister, the Navy Minister, and other cabinet members and prominent figures from both the government and the public will also attend. (Domei, 22nd)

The Truth About the Disturbances in Southern Xinjiang (Special Dispatch from Kashgar) 105

Turkic Leaders Mutually Slaughtering Each Other

Thousands of Han Chinese Suffer Abuse

Soviet Russia's Attitude is Highly Suspicious

Eagerly Awaiting Decisive Action from the Central Government

The discovery of a puppet government in Kashgar, Southern Xinjiang, has been reported by various foreign news agencies. However, due to transportation obstacles, the truth is unknown. The following is a report from a gentleman who has resided in Kashgar for over twenty years, which is both detailed and accurate, and includes several attached photos, which will be published successively. The people of the country who care about the border territories should not ignore this.

Timur, the Turkic leader in Kashgar, was originally a trusted follower of Hoja Niyaz (who held out in Hami), the overall Turkic leader of Xinjiang. When he came to Kashgar with the Muslims, he was entrusted with the important mission of establishing a purely Turkic Eastern Turkestan state. However, he soon had the intention of dividing power with the Muslim leader Ma Zhancang and resolving the power of the Hui people (stationing Ma Zhancang in the Han city, i.e., Shule). However, because his strength was not sufficient and the Turkic people were a cowardly rabble, while the Muslims were all warlike and fearless and their weapons were sharp and bullets abundant, he brewed for many days but ultimately dared not trigger the opportunity. Communication between Kashgar and Shule was therefore not interrupted. Similarly, Imir Pasha, the leader of Hotan (Pasha means Turkic King), also harbored this idea, but dared not try it. As for Ma Zhancang's strength, although it exceeded theirs, he was only strong enough to defend one city, and not enough to attack other places. Thus, the Turkic and Hui people in the Kashgar and Hotan regions were divided into three forces, each unwilling to yield to the other. Later, Timur, with his ambition to establish an Eastern Turkestan state, secretly incited the general low-class and ignorant Arabs, Afghans, Andijanis (Russian subjects), and local bandits who stayed in Kashgar, as well as the Ahongs (Turkic religious leaders) and Maulanas (Turkic chanters) who had always been hostile to the Han people, to conspire and offer advice, saying that this was right and that was wrong, slandering each other, creating an extremely chaotic situation. However, one noteworthy event was the destruction of Han Chinese temples and the establishment of two model schools, with all the faculty and staff being Arabs and Andijanis. The curriculum was newly compiled, and the content was nothing more than "Destroy the Han and Revive the Turkic" and various fallacies such as "Strive forward and it will not be difficult to occupy all of China." According to reliable information, this rebellion by the Turkic and Hui people was purely the result of cunning schemes, and was not incited by the Han people. However, disputes soon arose within their party, dark tides erupted, and the struggle for power was extremely fierce. Thus, Ma Shaowu, who had previously been placed under house arrest by Timur in the Hui city (Shufu), took the opportunity to mobilize the bandit leader Usman to defect. At that time, Usman was the brigade commander under Timur and had long coveted the position of division commander, but Timur monopolized the positions of division commander and commander, so Usman harbored deep resentment towards Timur. Ma Shaowu also secretly agreed with Ma Zhancang in the Han city (Shule) to provide assistance. On August 9th, they lured and killed Timur outside the city of Shufu. Ma Shaowu immediately sank to the Han city that day. At this time, the Hui city was taken by Ma Zhancang. Ma Shaowu had information about taking the stage, but it was not realized. The Hui city was soon occupied by the fickle Usman and the remnants of Timur's forces (at that time, August 16th, it was a joint effort between the Turkic people inside and outside). At this time, Usman monopolized the positions of division commander and commander. However, Usman was originally a mountain bandit, and his ambition was to obtain more money and Han Chinese women. Therefore, regardless of the advantages and disadvantages, he repeatedly ordered his troops to besiege the Han Chinese city, but the Han Chinese city was able to preserve itself because of the Han Chinese's efforts to defend it. Unfortunately, Ma Zhancang was both brutal and did not receive enough extorted money, and hated the Han Chinese for not doing "Namaz" (the name of a Hui Muslim prayer), so he still often abused and killed Han Chinese. Some Han Chinese who feared disaster fled, but were often killed by the Turkic people. This is truly painful. However, communication between the two cities has been cut off since then and has not been restored to this day. Usman and Ma Zhancang's troops also separately extorted huge sums of money from wealthy merchants inside and outside the city. Their subordinates, in groups of three or five, went to the countryside to plunder people's property, and not a few villagers were hanged by them under false pretenses. As a result, panic arose in people's hearts, and those with wealth fled to India one after another. However, the Han Chinese were no different from rats in a hole, daring not risk their lives to escape, but only hiding to avoid being killed. Before long, Usman was overthrown by Setivaldiang (an Andijani). Setivaldiang was a cloth merchant in Kashgar. During Timur's time, he served as the head of the national regiment. His hatred of the Han Chinese was no less than that of Usman. After Usman was overthrown, he swept away more than a hundred boxes of property he had plundered from the Han Chinese (and thirty or forty kidnapped women) and fled into the mountains overnight. He was soon arrested and imprisoned in the camp by Setivaldiang. At this time, the Hui city had no leader. Setivaldiang took this opportunity to organize a puppet government, with Sa Wudi Da Maulana (from Atush, a town one station away from the Hui city, a place where Han Chinese were never allowed to trade) as the leader. The old military and political figures, with Setivaldiang having the greatest power, were able to remain in their positions, while all others were replaced. A ceremony was held inside and outside the city to hang the false new national flag. The false flag was green and modeled after the Turkish style, which was quite enthusiastic for a time, causing a commotion throughout the city. However, they were all ignorant people. Observing their rise and fall, they have plunged Southern Xinjiang (the general term for the southern route of Tianshan) into a state of anarchy for more than seven months. The thousands of Han Chinese refugees who were not completely killed by the Turkic and Hui people are now groaning and waiting to be rescued from the fire pit. What is even more strange is that during this long period of turmoil, there has been no news of any measures taken by the Xinjiang Provincial Government, and not even a bit of information can be obtained, as if they had turned a blind eye and a deaf ear. I don't know what their intentions are. However, the Turkic newspapers recorded that Liu and Sheng of the provincial government had transferred Southern Xinjiang (Yanqi, Aksu, Kashgar, and Khotan four districts) to Hoja Niyaz to govern. This news came suddenly and was extremely frightening. However, there must be a reason for it. According to reliable sources, Hoja Niyaz is now in Aksu negotiating with Soviet Russia for a large amount of military supplies, such as airplanes and fast guns, in exchange for wool, which is transported by the Kazi of Ushi (a county name, one station away from Aksu, connected to the Russian-owned Hala Lake). At the same time, the puppet government in Kashgar is also sending Arabs with huge sums of money to India to buy airplanes, and Imir Pasha of Hotan is also exchanging Hotan silk with Afghanistan for armaments. What do they want to do by preparing so eagerly? This is worth noting. Furthermore, Soviet Russia, disregarding international friendship, is providing them with military supplies. What is its intention? This is even more worthy of study. The central government urgently needs to quickly find a way to deal with the situation. In general, this kind of turmoil cannot be quelled without the use of force by the central government, and the sooner the better. If they hesitate again, the thousands of miles of fertile land will surely become a detached territory, and the thousands of Han Chinese refugees with no way out will be forever trapped in the fire pit. Therefore, it is deeply hoped that the central government will adopt decisive measures, without further considering everything, and quickly send a large number of elite troops into Xinjiang to quell the rebellion. As for the road to Xinjiang, if it is impossible to negotiate with Soviet Russia, then the Dunhuang small road can also be used to copy to Hotan (it can arrive in 23-24 days, but there is a shortage of water), or you can take a long-distance bus from Guihua to Guchengzi (Qitai county name, six stations away from Dihua, it only takes six or seven days by bus), both are possible. As long as the central army arrives, the lost land can be expected to be recovered. If it is delayed any longer, it will give them the opportunity to collude with other countries, creating a more complex and difficult to resolve situation, and the same mistakes as the four northeastern provinces will surely be repeated. (Sent on December 28th)

General Situation of Hululu Wang Territory (Continued) 106

(1) Report from Cheng Fu Xing Regarding the Investigation of Mining Affairs

Respectfully submitting for your consideration: I, your humble servant, was ordered to investigate the mining affairs of Ban Hong, to announce the government's benevolent intentions, and to invite the Tusi chiefs to the provincial capital for discussions. Following this order, I departed from the provincial capital on January 10th of the 22nd year [of the Republic] and arrived at Mengning County City on February 2nd. I delayed for several days to prepare everything necessary for the journey and to invite local gentry familiar with the area to serve as advisors. On February 14th, I set off from Mengning. The journey to Gengma, being within our territory, was relatively easy and has already been reported. However, the route from Gengma through Mengyi to the Hululu Wang territory, though not long in distance, is inhabited by various ethnic groups with whom communication is difficult. The roads are treacherous and arduous, beyond description. Moreover, the areas along the way have, since ancient times, practiced the barbaric custom of taking human heads as sacrifices for good harvests. During the second or third and seventh or eighth months of the lunar calendar, the local people are more ferocious than usual, everyone carrying sharp long knives, honed like snow, never letting them out of their grasp, wielding them at the slightest provocation as if it were commonplace. Even Han Chinese merchants who normally trade in the area dare not travel during this period. When I arrived at Gengma, it was precisely the time of the Lang Umbrella headhunting season. The Tusi chiefs were terrified, as if they had seen a tiger, fearing that I would not return, and repeatedly tried to dissuade me. However, considering the importance of this matter to the entire financial lifeline of Yunnan and the great expectations of the government, I had no reason to retreat in the face of difficulty. Therefore, I summoned my courage and embarked on this exploratory journey. The accompanying gentry, such as Li Guiting, Li Fengting, and Qiu Daru from Mengning, and Wang Qidong from Shuangjiang, were all men of great courage and determination, willing to take risks to fulfill the mission and repay the government. The Tusi chiefs were greatly impressed. Han Fuguo, the Tusi chief of Gengma, seeing my determination to proceed, sent two soldiers and a squad leader to escort me, and also sent a letter written with burnt offerings to Hu Yushan, the Ban Hong Wang, to facilitate the investigation of mining affairs. I then proceeded directly to Mengdong Jiao. There, the Tusi chief Han Huaxiang also tried to intimidate me with the dangers ahead and tried to stop me from proceeding. The officers and soldiers sent by Gengma were also apprehensive. Fortunately, the Mengning and Shuangjiang gentry, Li, Qiu, Peng, and others, were deeply familiar with the border situation and had long been eager to assist the government in managing the frontier. They encouraged each other with the saying, "How can you catch a tiger cub without entering the tiger's den?" and volunteered to be the vanguard, which helped maintain stability. Seeing my fearlessness, Han Huaxiang also sent a relative to lead several men to accompany me, and also wrote a letter to the Ban Hong Wang. At this time, not only were the Kawa tribesmen rampant, but the Yellow bandits led by Fa Qing were also actively causing trouble, disturbing the borders of Ban Hong. As soon as I entered the territory, I received a letter from the Ban Hong Wang, saying that the Yellow bandits led by Fa Qing were attacking him, that all places were heavily guarded, and that he feared misunderstandings and requested that I not proceed. When I arrived at Ban Hong, they refused to open the寨gate. I then asked the Mengdong 新 Lord who accompanied me to reply with a letter, saying that I was the same Commissioner Li who had come before, sent by the government, traveling thousands of miles, and sent my seal and official documents, and also sent generous gifts. Seeing the seal and official documents, the Wang no longer refused and opened the gate to let me in. This was on February 20th. In total, excluding delays along the way, there were 21 stations from the province to Mengning, 2 stations from Mengning to Shuangjiang, 2 stations from Shuangjiang to Gengma, 2 stations to Mengjiao Dong, and 2 stations from Mengjiao Dong to Ban Hong, for a total of 29 stations. This is the journey from the province to Ban Hong. Upon arriving at Ban Hong, I first announced the government's benevolent intentions and distributed gifts. Then, I discussed with the Ban Wang the government's intention to open a mining factory in the area. The Ban Wang said, "I am originally a subject of the Great Qing Dynasty, and I have always obeyed the Great Qing government. It is acceptable to open this factory, but this factory does not belong to me alone. Besides Ban Hong, there are also Ban Lao Mine, Bie Yong, Banshao, and Xin Si Wang. It would be appropriate to proceed according to the precedents set by Wu Shangxian in ancient times." I then asked what those precedents were. The Ban Wang said, "The government must first notify all the Wangs, explaining the reasons for opening the factory. After the Wangs agree, the government must give dozens of sets of clothes, silver knives, saddles, and horses to the Wangs and headmen. They should all be invited to Ban Lao to gather, slaughter dozens of cattle, entertain the Wangs and headmen, and sign a contract. Only then can the factory be opened without obstacles. This is what was done effectively in the past." I then asked him to send someone to guide me to the mining area so that I could conduct an on-site inspection. The Ban Wang said that it was still difficult to do so because he had not yet communicated the reasons for the investigation to the Wangs, nor had he sent gifts to them to gain their favor. Going there rashly would be dangerous. I found the Wang's words to be honest and considerate. Although the Ban Wang had not read Han Chinese books, he spoke fluent Chinese and greatly admired Zhuge Wuhou (a pair of Kongming bronze drums still exists in Bang Nong). He was familiar with 茿 script and could recite Sanskrit scriptures, truly a wise and capable man. Although I knew that the Wang's words were sincere, there was no reason to return empty-handed after entering a mountain of treasure. Moreover, having been ordered to investigate, it would be a dereliction of duty not to conduct an on-site inspection of the mine. I still did not take a large retinue, but only accompanied the gentry from Mengning and Shuangjiang, Li, Qiu, Peng, and others, along with the Ban Hong Wang's son and a few attendants, totaling about a dozen people, traveling in disguise to dispel the suspicions of the Wangs. The journey from Ban Hong to the mine was over towering mountains, with steep cliffs and dense forests, rarely trod by human feet. We climbed vines and creepers, crossing dangerous cliffs and precipices, enduring all kinds of hardships before reaching the mine entrances. There were dozens of entrances, some tens of丈 deep and others more than ten丈. We inspected each entrance. The entrances were covered with bat droppings. The bats were almost as large as orioles. There was the sound of flowing water inside, with stone benches and stone bridges. When illuminated by electric light, the ore sparkled and shone brightly. The traces of prosperous management in the past were obvious, truly a sight to behold. Eventually, the sun was setting, and there was no place to stay. It was impossible to delay any longer, so we selected ore from the cave to be taken back in three categories for testing. The mountain area is about 9,230 square li or more, spanning the territories of five Wangs. Furthermore, the climate is mild, without mountain fog and瘴poison. No wonder it is famous throughout the world. After leaving the cave, we took photographs across the river. Along the road, we saw a　　going through, its trunk was great, in camp Hululu Wang land　mountain shape map

Making a foot seven feet or more, then photographed its image, to see a class of barbaric peoples, returned to Ban Hong, passed through Nan Village and consulted with the heads, first made a contract, so that this hard work, not to no avail, each head all agreed, then arrived at Ban Hong, then the king has invited the representatives of the kings, came before me etc., Under the interview, they all claimed that the Han Dynasty must come to start the business before it can be done, otherwise, we must unite the kings to do our best to resist, and never give up easily, and we must follow the precedents of Wu Shangxian in the past, etc., and the partners took out the government's official documents and seals, and then each agreed to obey, and they were willing to make a contract with the job first, as the basis for future investigative committees, and their intentions were extremely sincere, and it was difficult to refuse their request, so they established the future investigation, and made a contract, Gai Yi sexual many doubts, if it is not so, it is not enough to strengthen his faith in the heart of the government. The representatives of the kings are not easy to gather, and the Han Dynasty must come to open the office, and if it is not the Han Dynasty, they must do their best to resist, and they want it to be like this, and now they get it unintentionally, what a joy, this is the real situation of arriving at Ban Hong, personally visiting the mine, conducting field investigations, and discussing methods with each representative (below omitted). A rough diagram of the shape of the ore mountain is shown above.

(2) Memorandum Outlining Preparatory Measures for Developing the Hululu Wang Territory Silver Mine

Respectfully submitting for your consideration and instructions: I, your humble servant, have investigated the Hululu Wang territory silver mine and have already submitted a detailed report on the process for your consideration. Furthermore, I received instructions from the Governor to devise measures for commencing development. I have investigated the production quantity and quality of the Hululu Wang territory silver mine. Past history and various investigations can prove that its reputation has long been established, and there is no need for me to repeat it. However, the current opening, how to raise funds to set up factories, how to mine, refine, transport, and sell, are all technical problems. It requires individuals with mining knowledge and good planning skills to personally visit the site and work practically to avoid the drawbacks of building a cart behind closed doors and cutting one's toes to fit the shoes. Therefore, for the sake of seeking truth from facts, I propose to start with a preparatory committee. On the one hand, it should enlist the support of the three Tusi chiefs of Gengma, Mengdian, and Mengdong Jiao, as well as the five Wangs of Ban Hong, so that they have a high degree of trust in our government, so as to eliminate actual obstacles. On the other hand, it should enlist talented individuals with border affairs aspirations, mining knowledge, and interests, so that they have opportunities to contact the local people of the Hululu Wang territory, so as to investigate and design. For this reason, I propose that the province commission several specialists, who I will guide to the Hululu Wang territory, to act as a preparatory committee, to liaise with the Tusi chiefs and to plan and implement on site. If success is foreseeable and there is certainty, then organize a Hululu Wang Territory Mining Affairs Committee to formally commence development. After careful consideration, I have drafted preparatory work steps and the organizational charter of the Ban Hong Mining Affairs Committee, each in one copy. I hereby respectfully submit this document to the Governor for your consideration. Would it be possible to select specialists and issue preparatory funds to be guided by me to the Hululu Wang territory for on-site planning and implementation? I humbly request your approval and instructions. Respectfully submitted by Li, Director of the Fudian New Bank, and Li Jingsen, investigator of the Hululu Wang territory mining affairs.

(3) Outline of Preparations for Developing the Hululu Wang Territory Silver Mine

(1) Request for the appointment of preparatory personnel: 1. Two factory affairs preparatory committee members, who must have mining and metallurgy knowledge, are responsible for surveying the mining area, testing the ore quality, and designing mining and refining matters. 2. Two administrative committee members, who must be familiar with the border situation and have talented scholars, plan all mining matters and are responsible for communicating government intentions, liaising with Tusi chiefs and headmen, and investigating the political, economic, racial, religious, language, and other living conditions of the factory site. 3. Eight preparatory committee members are proposed to be commissioned to the three Tusi chiefs of Gengma, Mengdian, and Mengdong Jiao, as well as the five Wangs of Ban Hong, in order to facilitate liaison and promote progress.

(2) Determine the mining area: 1. After arriving in the Hululu Wang territory, immediately survey the mines and test the ore quality. 2. If the ore quality is excellent and there is a possibility of trial operation, select the most prosperous vein with the best components as the factory site. 3. At the same time, investigate the culture and living conditions.

(3) Trial factory establishment: 1. Build ten simple houses, each requiring about 200 yuan in cash, for a total of 2,000 yuan in cash. 2. Install five old-style furnaces, each requiring about 500 yuan in cash, for a total of 2,500 yuan. 3. Temporarily employ 50 sand workers, hired from neighboring counties, each ten workers supplying one furnace, each person earning 70 cents in silver cash per day, totaling 35 yuan per day and 1,050 yuan per month. 4. Purchase 50 sets of mining tools and explosives (one axe, one hoe, one hammer, roughly like sappers), each set costing about 10 yuan in cash, for a total tool cost of 500 yuan in cash. The explosives purchase requires 200 yuan in cash, and ten cannons need 100 yuan in cash, for a total of 800 yuan in cash. 5. Hire technicians, one person for each furnace, for a total of three people, with a monthly salary estimated at 50 yuan in cash, for a total of 150 yuan in cash. 6. Open a charcoal factory, which can be opened in the mountains near the mine, about 20 to 30 li away, requiring 5,000 jin of charcoal to be burned daily, costing about 100 yuan in cash, or 3,000 yuan per month. 7. Organize provisions, which are purchased and transported from the lands of the three Tusi chiefs of Gengma, Mengdian, and Mengdong Jiao, requiring about 100 jin of rice per day, estimated at 13 yuan in cash for 100 people, or about 500 yuan per month, for a total of 1,000 yuan. 8. Organize ten transport animals, camels and mules, each costing 200 yuan in cash, for a total cost of 2,000 yuan (temporary hires are not included). 9. Estimate the cost of trial factory establishment to be over 12,000 yuan, with regular expenses of about 5,000 yuan. It is expected that a monthly income of four hands of silver bars will result in a surplus.

(4) Promote the Mining Affairs Committee: 1. When the trial factory is decided to be established, the administrative committee members must formally organize the administrative office, handle reporting, publicity, application for funds, and distribution of uses. 2. After one month of operation, report the factory conditions and output to the province for verification. If it is considered that it can be continued, try again for one month, and then formally establish a Mining Affairs Committee in accordance with the organizational charter, and establish a factory police team for protection. At this point, the preparatory work is completed, and the government formally appoints the mining affairs committee members and managers, responsible for planning improvements, and determining supervisory regulations to guide them.

(5) Preparations for departure: 1. Purchase chemical reagents for testing and local mining equipment. 2. Purchase gifts for慰慰 the Tusi chiefs and Tusi kings. 3. Create survey forms and all stationery. 4. Request the preparatory and travel expenses.

(Addendum) The slag from the smelting of ore by Wu Shangxian in the past is piled up like mountains in dozens of places. The old silver factory near Ban Hong, Myanmar, due to the exhaustion of raw materials in recent years, the manager of the factory, Wu Bolan, has purchased this tribute ore slag from the Bang Nong tenant officials at any time and transported it to Mengyao. Excluding hired porters, each 100 jin is settled at a price of 10 English Yang. Now, if we independently operate the raw ore, we can contact the old silver factory and sell this ore slag. The profit can be used as the regular expenses of the factory each year.

Suzhou 109

The Jiangsu Province Touring Station Decided to be Located on Tiger Hill in Suzhou

Chairman Chiang Kai-shek launched　the Southeast Transportation Touring Exhibition, scheduled to begin on June 15th, lasting 20 days. Participants included five provinces: Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Anhui, Fujian, and Jiangxi. Each province selected a key transportation hub to establish a exhibition site, serving as a touring station, displaying products and transportation equipment along the highways. Besides Zhejiang, which was set up at Mount Tianmu and Mount Yandang, and Jiangxi, which was set up at Mount Longhu, the locations for Fujian and Anhui had not been determined. Jiangsu Province, however, was designated as a key transportation route due to its rich products and beautiful scenery, so the touring station was decided to be located on Tiger Hill in Suzhou. The county government has been ordered to rush to complete the Su-Chang Road so that the highways of the five provinces can connect to Fujian and Jiangxi via the Xi-Chang, Xi-Hu, Xi-Yi, and Jing-Wu roads. On one side, from Suzhou Su-Jia road reaches Hangzhou, and then Shanghai from Hu-Hang road, will be connected before the exhibition, unobstructed. County Magistrate Zou is also planning to rebuild Tiger Hill Road to enhance the views.

Dispute at the Vegetable Market Resolved 110

The dispute at the Xilikou Vegetable Market on Fuzhou Street, due to both sides holding their ground, has been suspended for several months without resolution. Now, the Second District Office and others have taken on the role of mediator, convening representatives of various vegetable merchants to discuss and decide to formally move into the market on March 1st to conduct business. The county government has also ordered the Public Security Bureau to prohibit the establishment of vegetable stalls on Fuzhou Street and the street in front from that day onwards.

Investigation of the Xu-Ge Lawsuit Begins 111

Xu Yunxiu, the former Chinese secretary of Soochow University, has recently been sued by Ge, a woman from Changshu, to the Wuxian District Court for abandonment. Yesterday morning at 9:00 AM, Prosecutor Du Jiasheng of the District Prosecutor's Office opened a court hearing. The defendant, Xu Yunxiu, as well as Xu's second wife, Zhang Guizhen, and Xu Enqi, were not present due to other matters. The plaintiff, Ge, had arrived in Suzhou from her old residence in Changshu to await the hearing. Witnesses Ge Kunxiang (who served as the媒for Ge's marriage to Xu), Xu Shao (Ge's sister-in-law), and clansmen Xu Qian, Xu Qunlian, and others, as well as the plaintiff's lawyer, Liu Zuwang, were also summoned. The hearing lasted for three hours. Ge stated the suffering of being abandoned by Yunxiu for forty years, and that her son, Xu Enqi, who is now a professor at Soochow University, also did not fulfill his obligation to support her, and requested that the court punish him with the due punishment. Xu Yunxiu claimed that he had divorced Ge long ago, severing the relationship between husband and wife, and therefore could not be considered abandonment. Witnesses Xu Qian, Xu Shao, and Ge Kunxiang, among others, testified that Ge and Yunxiu had not divorced. Xu Junkang testified that they had divorced. After the questioning, both the plaintiff and the defendant were dismissed and asked to await a scheduled rehearing.

Wuxi 112

Labor Dispute at Qingfeng Textile Mill

The Qingfeng Textile Mill in Zhoushan浜, Wuxi, has been in operation for over ten years. The factory stopped on December 27th of the old lunar year and was originally scheduled to resume work on the seventh day of the first lunar month. However, the factory intends to reform the management aspect from this year onwards, replacing male workers in the steel wire machine section with female workers. The First Factory workshop originally had more than sixty male workers, who were all dismissed by Factory Director Tang at the end of the old year. Before yesterday was the start of reopening, dismissed workers, believing that they would be unemployed and have difficulty making a living, held incense sticks and went to the factory, requesting the board of directors and supervisors of the factory union office to serve as mediators. However, they were rejected by the factory and not allowed to enter, leading to a riot. Workers in the steel wire department went on strike. Fearing that the matter would escalate, the factory immediately reported to the Sixth Branch of the Public Security Bureau and the county police patrol team, which dispatched teams to the site to suppress the situation. The workers were helpless and dispersed. That night, over two thousand workers at the old factory went on strike en masse. However, the dismissed workers were unwilling to give up and proposed nine conditions to cope with the situation: 1. Reinstate the two workers who were dismissed without cause (those dismissed after December 28th of the old lunar year). 2. Piecework wages must be paid on time and not withheld. 3. Reinstate the night meal allowance. 4. Wages should be paid monthly as before and not changed to daily pay. 5. Reinstate the worship salary: machine workers and female workers are paid full wages for the first week. 6. Restore the reduced wages. 7. Improve treatment, extend meal times, remove cold water for rinsing rice, the leather rod room still belongs to the old factory, machine workers have freedom to eat, and restore stools. Factory Director Tang must not arbitrarily beat people in the future. 8. Re-employ Ding Qian, the former chief manager, and reject engineer Li Xin. 9. All of the above eight articles must be accepted by the factory before work can resume. The workers petitioned the county party headquarters on one hand and went to the Textile Union on the other, requesting mediation. Yesterday (the 22nd), the union held an emergency meeting to discuss mediation methods. As a result, a representative was selected to petition the county government. After arriving at the county, County Magistrate Yan came out to meet them and instructed the representatives to persuade the workers to resume work first. In the afternoon, more workers went to the county party headquarters to petition first, and then went to the county government to petition. County Magistrate Yan met with the representatives and instructed the striking workers to resume work first. All sixty dismissed people will quietly wait for the party and government agencies to discuss a resolution. The six representatives were satisfied and agreed to inform the workers to resume work this morning (the 23rd) and await the resolution today.
