Free Talk

On Beating 220

— Xu Maoyong

Looking at the theories of the new educators, most of them do not advocate the use of corporal punishment on elementary school students, but in reality, I don't know if elementary school students are still being hit on the palms by teachers now? If they are not anymore, then they are really happy, making those of us who studied ten years earlier envious.

Ten years ago, no elementary school student escaped being hit on the palm, and no matter how fiercely the teacher beat, parents and others would never say a word. We had a folk song that said:

"Parents beat, it is right to beat; teacher beats, paid to (him) beat; others beat, report to the Baozhang (i.e., Baozheng)."

Originally, the teacher's beating of students meant that the students paid for him to beat them. Why pay him to beat them? Probably because since ancient times, studying was for becoming an official, and officials could beat people. If you didn't study well, you couldn't become an official, and if you didn't become an official, you couldn't beat people. But to study well, you had to ask the teacher to supervise you strictly, and the strictest supervision was beating. Being beaten by the teacher meant that in the future, when you became an official, you could beat back on the people many times over, which was just like needing to invest capital first to earn interest.

Therefore, Chinese people in the past were all inevitably beaten by their parents, those who studied were beaten by their teachers, and those who didn't study were either beaten by officials, or by foremen, or by landlords...

We can say that those who have never been beaten cannot be considered Chinese.

I recently saw the following passage in the "Travels in China" by the Spanish literary giant Blasco Ibáñez:

"For five thousand years, that hard bamboo board has been the true authority in China. That magic board forces people to obey moral laws and operates the machinery of the country. Among the Chinese, the only person who will not be beaten is the emperor. In addition, even the most honorable officials or trusted favorites are inevitably beaten a dozen or twenty times under the emperor's orders to atone for their mistakes. After being beaten, they can still resume their old positions when the emperor expresses sympathy for them. A Chinese person, from childhood, is accustomed to being beaten by his parents, so no one is ashamed of being beaten a few times in their life. If they commit a fault, as long as they get a beating, their rice bowl will not be completely broken, and their power will not be reduced. They see being beaten as lightly as we see being fined by the city government. The Chinese police always carry bamboo sticks or whips in their hands, and immediately beat the people when they see them committing a crime."

Foreigners often exaggerate when talking about the unique aspects of China. This passage, at first glance, seems a bit exaggerated, but it is actually true. Even today, the situation of beating and being beaten is still like this. It's just that people don't necessarily use bamboo boards to beat people, but also palms, fists, leather shoes, gun butts, shoe soles, opium pipes... anything is possible, and the spectacle is imaginable!

Chinese Humor 221

— Shi Heng

I have said that the Chinese nation is not suitable for humor, because all so-called literature has almost always been controlled by the scholar-official class, and the atmosphere of the scholar-official class is the most anti-humorous. Occasionally, in the literature of the common people, we can see things similar to humor, but it is more appropriate to call that banter than humor, because in this banter there is a kind of vulgarity hidden, which cannot be compared with the intellectual metaphors we commonly call humor; on the contrary, this banter is extremely close to the vulgar, glib talk of the crosstalk performers in general variety shows, and perhaps the currently popular crosstalk has developed from the banter in the literature of the common people.

In the literature of the common people, this kind of banter is often inappropriately inserted in order to maintain the interest of the readers. Strictly speaking, it is harmful to the integrity of the art, but when we understand the author's intention, we are not too critical, and we might as well laugh along with the author. As for those ordinary readers, when they read such places, they will laugh heartily.

In books like "Three Heroes and Five Gallants," there are quite a few such examples. To understand what Chinese banter is, let's look at one or two examples. In the thirty-fifth chapter, it is written that Feng Junheng glanced at his cousin, and then the author bantered to explain it:

"He said that a single glance was inhuman, no human would glance like that. Often books often say "eyes and eyebrows convey affection," and also say "eyebrows come, eyes go." Thinking carefully, this eyebrow is useless, the eyes are for looking; the eyebrows follow behind. What's the point of stirring? Isn't that what they say? If it didn't have it, it would be really ugly. It's just like the joke says 丨丨 the mouth said to the nose: "Hey, old nose! What ability do you have to dare to live above me?" The nose slowly said: "If you didn't rely on me to smell, how would you distinguish between fragrance and foulness?" The nose also spoke to the eyes: "Cure, old eyes! What ability do you have to dare to live above me?" The eyes replied: "If you didn't rely on me to see, how would you know what's good or bad?" The eyes also spoke to the eyebrows: "Hey, old eyebrows! What ability do you have to dare to live above me?" The eyebrows replied: "I originally didn't have any ability, but I'm just your matching accessory. If you don't want me to be above you, then move to the bottom of you. See if you look like something or not. 丨丨 Feng Jun rushed his glance, really put the eyebrows in the wrong place."

This, like all vulgar, glib talk, is a disguised form of scolding; at the same time, like all vulgar, glib talk, this scolding, if carefully considered, is not very appropriate. From this kind of banter, you can see the scholar-official atmosphere in the literature of the common people, because the scolding is already cleverly scolded, and this scholar-official atmosphere is easily accepted by the general uneducated common people, or in other words, is easily infected by it. Therefore, it is probably not wrong to say that the popular crosstalk entertainment in Chinese society was originally learned by the common people from the scholar-officials; however, once it reached the mouths of the common people, it became more and more vulgar, and as a result, it became a complete vulgar, glib talk.

From such banter, we can see a principle that banter is used to conceal scolding, which becomes what we call sarcasm or bitterness, and this laughter is not good laughter. However, sometimes, although it still does not escape the air of bitterness, there are also examples of banter that are not deliberately arranged by the author, but created through the depiction of customs and human feelings. This is most vividly depicted in the ninety-third chapter of "Continued Little Five Nurturings," which describes the poor grandfather's performance on the Lei Tai. Although the original text is longer, it is necessary to quote it in order to explain the style of Chinese humor.

It is said that this poor man was so poor that he was in such a plight, how could he have the heart to perform on the Lei Tai? All because everyone urged him, and it was truly out of helplessness... He was worried about Ma Long, and thinking in his heart about comparing his posture, there was a person behind him who taught him to elbow a somersault. That person crawled up, pounding his chest, and hummed, "Ouch, ouch," and said, "Friend! Look, it's about time to go and find something to eat. Look at us, we all have cold rice when we go home after watching the Lei Tai. It seems that you, sir, have to go and find something now; if you miss the time, who can prepare something so readily for you? I'm saying good things."

"This gentleman's qi rushed upwards, and he said, "It's up to me whether I go to find something or not, what does it have to do with you?" That person said, "I'm just suffering from a chronic illness, and you elbowed me in the heart: you don't care whether I can bear it or not! Look, there are many people watching the excitement, who is like you bringing a posture to fight? If you really have the ability, go up and compete with this Taiguan; if you can really kick this Taiguan like me, it's a thousand taels; hit him with a punch, and you'll get fifty taels, enough to change your clothes; what's the point of this!" The poor man said, "I don't like changing clothes, you can't meddle in my business!" That person said, "I can't meddle. No more words, I'm going to stand in front of you."

"It just so happened that the poor man saw Ma Ye throw a punch that didn't hit the mark, and he compared his posture again, saying, "If it's like this, I might hit the Taiguan." With a bang, he hit that person's back heart again. That person let out an ouch, and plunged forward, if there weren't so many people, he would have almost fallen down.

"That person turned his head and said fiercely, "You poor ghost! Are you crazy from being poor! I haven't dodged you back and forth. Since you have this ability, why don't you go up and show your face? You only know how to bully me!" The poor man said, "I'm using my strength for that friend." That person said, "If you use your strength for that person again, I'll die! You're a good friend, go up!" The poor man said, "I'll go up, I'll go up! It's a pity that I'm wearing tattered clothes now 丨" That person said, "It's not about the clothes; if you really have the ability, people will change your clothes for you. I'm just afraid you don't dare to go up." The poor man said, "You've said so much that I have to go up." That person said, "Very good!" The poor man looked at his clothes... and still didn't want to go up.

"That injured person was originally a bad person: he secretly arranged with a dozen people to squeeze the poor man up, everyone put in their efforts, shouted in unison, and said, "Grandpa Poor has arrived!" And squeezed the poor man onto the stage..."

Here, there seems to be no bitterness from the author himself, but it is written about vulgar, glib-talking people, and the article becomes banter. Compared to the previous example, there is a slight difference, but they are largely the same.

This kind of Chinese banter is still continuing in modern literature, only with a different name, called humor. However, humor always cannot be separated from vulgar, glib talk, and its future is quite dangerous.

"Going Out" 222

— Wei Mengke

I went to sleep amidst the crackling sounds, and woke up again amidst the crackling sounds, feeling half of my face hot, knowing that the sun had also risen. Today is New Year's Day.

Opening the east-facing window, a gust of wind brought in the smell of gunpowder, which made my head ache. Before me was a expanse of azure sea, the weather was so good!

After getting dressed, I took a handheld camera, wanting to "go out" early.

"Kill!...", just as I stepped out of the door, I heard a burst of sharp cries like magpies chirping beside my ears. A group of children, suddenly all dressed in new clothes, wearing red beards, and holding lacquered bright wooden swords and guns, were valiantly practicing a charge at the entrance of the alley.

The road was also quiet, the doors of the shops were tightly closed, and although there were many wonderful sayings on the red couplets, the red paper strips with "Let wealth be generated towards me" were all the same. The rumbling manure carts had all been cleared away. Only the "music team" that had appeared last night was still beating large gongs and drums, touring back and forth in one group after another. 丨 Although these heroes hadn't slept all night, the shared look of a smiling face proved that they were still in high spirits.

Walking, where to go, I didn't care. But then I encountered many new heroes. 丨丨 The performers were mostly wearing small melon-shaped caps, with long silk belts around their waists, the kind of characters who usually resolved disputes in the streets and alleys. Their pockets were full of "money crackers," treading softly, as if they were investigating who was there. If they encountered a Miss, they would think it was a great discovery, hurry to chase after her, and throw a handful on the ground, with a loud bang, everyone would laugh heartily. I heard that the Misses of Shanghai do not take their Pekingese dogs out for a walk on New Year's Day, and that is indeed reasonable.

Walking. Before me, iron wire nets were spread out, which startled me at this time, but I immediately realized that I was going to the "Chinese territory". Here, the iron wire nets were laid out on a small river, which is what is called a Ham by the people of Shanghai. Although this Ham was narrow, it was crowded with dozens of large and small grass boats. Golden-colored rice straw was stacked on the boat cups, looking from afar like countless earthen hills. Through the gaps between the boats, you could faintly see the purplish-brown mud kissing the boat's belly. 丨 The water having dried up in the winter, the farmers also actually had the opportunity to spend the New Year in this prosperous Shanghai! Most of the boats were inserted with three incense sticks and a pair of red candles, and some also set off a few strings of firecrackers, which was naturally to pray to the gods for protection, to sell those rice straws quickly, and to load a boat of fertilizer to take back when the spring tide rose. Didn't they spend their blood and sweat to earn all of that this year! Women were cooking at the stern of the boat, and smoke was everywhere. The children were rolling in the straw piles, making a fuss and laughing happily. Although none of them had new clothes to wear, they were always happy, it was the New Year!

Walking out of the iron gate, crossing the arched stone bridge, it was still a road, but there were no more skyscrapers, dried trees, withered yellow weeds, and abandoned fields, and also, there were rotten coffins, with the stench of corpses filling the air, lying scattered on the soil, which was probably beneficial to farming, although or to hygiene...? No, this was the countryside.

It is said that people who have lived in the city for a long time are bound to find everything lovely when they occasionally set foot in the countryside, but unfortunately, I was surrounded by countless beggars, unable to stroll freely.

When I turned back, the sun was overhead, and the breeze brought the sound of du du du, which was the factory's whistle for the workers to get off work. It must be time for the people who still had to work even during the New Year to rest, but the beggars still followed me closely, chasing after me, and also celebrating along the way, saying, "Sir, congratulations on making a fortune in the New Year!"

Interesting Metaphors 223

— Shu

(18)

You Xitang (Dong)'s "Miscellany" is a masterpiece in the genre of notebook novels. Xitang was, of course, also a famous scholar in literature and history. However, people only know him as a famous scholar, and do not know that he was once a lavish but poor literati. I once saw a letter of his to a friend, in which he said: "The year is coming to an end, the wind and rain are bleak! Paper windows and bamboo tails, the lamplight is green, I do not know where the beauty lies. The wild goose fur is ordinary, where is the lone sable? The fish pot is empty, where is the lamb? An ancient poet said: The wind wants to freeze the wine, the frost can break the cotton. Now there is no wine to freeze, no cotton to break, alas, alas, how to end the year?" When we read this in the lament of "how to end the year," we truly have some "real heart," the happiness is bitter, but there is interest in the bitterness, so I have attached it to the end of the interesting metaphors.

(19)

The above "Interesting Metaphors" are seventeen items. They were written when reading Zhou Liangong's "Collected from the Lai Gutang Correspondence," twelve volumes, Second Collection of "Hidden and Discarded Collection," sixteen volumes, Third Collection of "Neighborhood Collection," sixteen volumes. The reason for publishing them is just to elicit a smile from the readers in this painful year! The narrowness of the literary path lately is beyond words. I was neither born with the bones of a Westernized writer, nor can I fill my hungry stomach with the clear breeze and bright moon. I had no choice but to seek this bitter interest, and I truly have a feeling of crying and laughing. May the magnanimous and refined men of today understand me. Postscript on February 10, 1933.

I Curse That Smile of Yours (9) 224

— Wu Yan

Outside the bamboo cage surrounding the racetrack, the gray highway for trade with Yunnan and Myanmar rose up, winding down from the mountains, and crawling up again like a snake. On the mimosa vines that spread along the roadside, two or three points of dark green fireflies flowed, and when touched with the electric light, they disappeared into the grass.

When the electric light shone into the dark and gloomy jungle on the slope, the little birds roosting in the branches called out in panic, shaking their brow-like wings, scattering into the moonlit sky. After a while, it returned to silence. The surrounding blue mountain layers were sleeping quietly, and the bare feet of the moonlight stepped over them without seeming to notice at all.

Only the Bilang River, running from the Chinese fields in the gorge, was still singing alone and passionately in the deep night, as if having escaped its hometown and come to a foreign land, it was very happy and excited.

Light from the lamp in Old Liu's house shone through the cracks in the bamboo wall. We, the two night wanderers searching for beautiful women, opened the bamboo door and walked in. The shadow of the wild woman, with her black cloth-wrapped head and large earrings, making shoes under the oil lamp, was painted crudely on the bamboo wall. She looked up, stunned for a moment, and after I greeted her, she smiled and asked in Chinese:

"What are you doing?"

She looked at the foreigner standing beside me, and a slightly surprised expression flowed out.

"He wants to check the people in this house to see if anyone is doing anything illegal."

I held back my laughter, deliberately using a very official tone to scare this usually unruly woman, while also trying to cover up this shameful thing, so that people wouldn't find out about it.

"Hehehe..."

"A strange laugh sounded from behind. Looking back, I didn't know when Old Liu had already been standing behind us. He hung down the corners of his mouth at me and smiled meaningfully, as if he was contemptuously saying 丨丨 Oh, you respectable young man! How come you're also doing the "pimping" thing? He said unhappily:

"Not a single Yi woman has come this evening!"

Needless to say, he was already preemptively guessing, just like my boss, and then said very angrily:

"Don't you have a lot of them in your shop?"

Looking at that kind of smile, hearing that kind of cold words, I was immediately annoyed. It was like being whipped heavily on the soul.

"It's none of my damn business, people are here to inspect!"

With my face flushed red, I reluctantly retorted, stuffed the flashlight to the foreigner, and angrily left alone.

When I got to the shop, I explained to the Indian man, and then went to sleep. As I took off my clothes, I suddenly thought:

"This is not right!"

Report on the Tianjin International Bicycle Race 236

Fourteen Miles in 45 Minutes 53.8 Seconds

New Page Added to Tianjin Sports History

(Tianjin Dispatch) The International Bicycle Race was held at Hedong on the afternoon of the 18th in strong winds, according to the original plan. 26 athletes participated, with one absent. The three foreigners all had

Excellent Vehicles. After gathering, they set off from the front of the Municipal Normal School, led by Liu Wei'en, with inspectors and doctors following in cars to check the race and provide medical assistance. The riders initially started very quickly. No. 19, Mu Xiangyue,

Took the Lead First, followed by the three Westerners, and No. 1, Wang Shudian, trailing behind. From the Municipal Normal School to Dazhigu, the journey was downwind, so everyone was able to increase their speed at will, keeping pace with the cars. However, the road conditions were not good, with many gravel and stones, and

Uneven Surfaces. The athletes worked hard and remained consistent throughout. The first to reach the finish line was No. 20, Austrian Weiss, but because he used improper methods to force No. 6, Shen Shijun, to the side of the road 20 meters from the finish line, the competition committee decided to

Disqualify Him and promote the second-place finisher. The original first-place finisher, No. 6, Shen Shijun, who unfortunately fell off his bike, and No. 13, Wang Ruixiang, who also fell off his bike due to being blocked by No. 20, Weiss, were both deemed to have performed well by the committee and were awarded souvenirs by the organizing committee. In total, the 14-mile journey was completed by the first-place finisher in 45 minutes and 53.8 seconds. The difference between the second-place finisher

Was Extremely Small, with a time of 45 minutes and 54.2 seconds. After the race, the awards were presented at the YMCA on Dongmalu at 4 PM. Zhao Wenzao delivered a speech, followed by Ruan Weijing giving out the awards. The meeting was adjourned. The first-place finisher received a domestically produced bicycle donated by Asian Motors, and the other two finalists received silver shields donated by Fengxiang Gold Store. The top ten finishers all received commemorative medals. The names of the top ten winning athletes are listed below:

Winners' Names: (1) Ma Diankui, (2) Mu Yue, (3) Mu Chengkui, (4) Jia Wenhe, (5) Zhou Wujie, (6) Zhao Shijie, (7) Erweier, (8) Li Shanhe, (9) Qi Qingfeng, (10) Gao Xien. The time of the first-place finisher was 45 minutes and 53.8 seconds, and the time of the second-place finisher was 45 minutes and 54.2 seconds.

Municipal Education Bureau Orders Elementary School Sports Days to Be Held in Spring in the Future 238

Secondary Schools to Be Held in Autumn

The Municipal Education Bureau, in order to change the elementary school sports days to be held in the spring and secondary school sports days to be held in the autumn from this year onwards, specially issued instructions to the municipal and registered private primary and secondary schools yesterday, stating that the Education Association of the Fifth District of the city reported that the joint sports days of the city's primary schools have always been held in the autumn, and due to the coldness and the length of the days, it is quite inconvenient for students in rural areas to participate. Because transportation in rural areas is difficult, participation in the conference requires timely attendance, which inevitably requires traveling to Shanghai the day before. Some are able to travel back and forth on the same day, but because the competition ends late, they cannot catch the last ferry at 5:00 PM at the Tongren Wharf and must stay overnight in Shanghai. Not only is there expense of food and lodging, but also the anxiety of families waiting, which reduces the interest in participating. It is better to hold it in late spring, March or April, when the weather is warm, everything is thriving, and children are lively, with plenty of time for transportation, so that schools in remote areas can also participate, in order to fully support the Bureau's advocacy of sports. According to this, the children's physical condition and climate are key factors for the joint sports days of primary schools, and it is more appropriate to hold them in the spring. The 179th Bureau Affairs Meeting of this Bureau resolved that elementary school sports days will be held in the spring and secondary school sports days will be held in the autumn from this year onwards. In addition to separate orders, this order is hereby issued to the school for notification. This order.

Jiangsu Provincial Local Education Supervision Conference Opened Yesterday 240

More Than 100 Attendees, Zhou Fohai Presided

First General Meeting Held at 2 PM

Zhenjiang, 22nd - The Jiangsu Provincial Local Education Supervision Conference convened by the Department of Education opened on the morning of the 22nd. More than 100 people attended, with Zhou Fohai presiding. First, Chen Guofu gave a speech on behalf of Cheng Tianfang, providing detailed instructions on the problems and improvements in local education. Then, Zhou Fohai explained the importance of the conference and gave instructions on the attitude and methods that supervision should take. Afterwards, the heads of various departments gave reports one after another. In the afternoon, the first meeting was held, and Cao Chumei and Xian Tai were appointed as chairman and vice-chairman respectively. Methods such as mutual exchange of supervision by county supervisors were adopted. Zhao, the Director of Finance, and Shen, the Director of Construction, along with Bo Ling and Jing Tang, two committee members, went to Haizhou on the 22nd to survey the Xugou Commercial Port and, on the way back, inspected the Datang River project.

The Jiangsu Provincial Department of Education convened a provincial local education supervision conference, which was held at the Department of Education at 9:00 AM yesterday (the 22nd). Approximately 110 people attended, including county supervisors, primary education instructors, principals of provincial normal schools, and Department of Education staff members related to local education. The opening ceremony was held in the morning, with speeches by Cheng Tianfang, Secretary-General of the Provincial Government, and Zhou Fohai, Director of the Department of Education, followed by free speeches by members. The first general meeting was held at 2:00 PM in the afternoon. The details are recorded below:

Attendees Yesterday: Department of Education Staff: Wu He, Ruan Zhidao, Chen Tianou, Xie Xin, Xie Jizeng, Chen Xifang, Yi Junzuo, Zhou Yuxin, Feng Ce, Jiang Zhuoqun, Deng Chuan, Shen Fu, Xue Zhongtai, Liu Baichuan, Jin Zonghua, Peng Daquan, Yi Zuolin, Yu Quntan, Cao Shutian, Xu Xihuang; Provincial Normal School Principals: Cao Chu, Shen Peixuan, Zheng Mian, Gu Kebin, Xu Tao, Cao Zhongquan, Yu Yu; Primary Instructors: Wang Zongjin, Chen Duo, Xin Zenghui, Wu Hengtong, Jiang Naixing, Xu Shoukang, Chen Tianma, Song Binggong, Hong Ji, Zhu Jingxing, Wang Xipeng, Wang Mingyu; and county supervisors, totaling more than 110 people. The ceremony was presided over by Zhou Fohai, Director of the Department of Education, and

Cheng Tianfang Gave a Speech, briefly stating, "Chairman Chen is going to Jiangxi on important business, so I will briefly speak to you. The foundation of education is built on primary schools. If primary schools are run well, then secondary schools can be run well. If secondary schools are good, then universities can be good. I have a few feelings about the current primary school education: (1) Primary school education is supposed to be compulsory, but this is not the case in China now. On the contrary, there is a problem of having too few schools and too many students; (2) There are not enough teachers. This is a common phenomenon everywhere, so we want to find ways to gradually increase rural normal schools; (3) The education industry is separated from the production industry. Often, before students are educated, they can still produce, but after being educated, they become members of the property division and despise working in rural areas. This is a serious and noteworthy issue for the future of Chinese education. Although Jiangsu's education funds are tight, they are relatively rich compared to other provinces. We certainly hope for an increase in education funds, but we must not take it from land taxes again. Rural areas are already on the verge of bankruptcy. Should we help them and maintain them, or should we increase their burden?"

Zhou Fohai's Speech briefly stated, "Today's local education supervision conference is the first of its kind in Jiangsu. Not only in Jiangsu, but also in the entire country, it has never been held before, so whether this conference will have results or achievements has a great impact on the future of education. I hope that you will pay special attention. The important issue of this conference is the mutual exchange of supervision by county supervisors. The key points are: (1) It can eliminate the drawbacks of local revenge and favoritism; (2) It can make supervisors nervous; (3) It can make those being supervised work harder; (4) It can improve the status of county supervisors, expand their powers, and increase their responsibilities. The key points that county supervisors should pay attention to are: (1) Rural textbooks; (2) Music textbooks; (3) Sports textbooks. All of these must have textbooks that promote the national spirit. Finally, I hope that all supervisors will be serious and fair, and not perfunctory."

Cao Chu and Others Gave Speeches At the end, Cao Chu, principal of Zhenjiang Normal School, was appointed as chairman, and Mei Zhaotai was appointed as vice-chairman. Then, Chen Xifang, Xiang Ju, Tan Cao, Cao Chu, and others gave speeches one after another. The meeting was adjourned after taking a photo.

Ministry of Education Announces Regulations for the Board of Directors of Overseas Chinese Primary and Secondary Schools 241

The Ministry of Education and the Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission jointly announced on the 21st the revised regulations for overseas Chinese primary and secondary schools (49 articles), the revised regulations for the registration of overseas Chinese schools (8 articles), and the revised regulations for the general meeting organization of overseas Chinese primary and secondary schools (14 articles). The revised regulations for the board of directors of overseas Chinese primary and secondary schools are recorded below: (Article 1) These regulations are revised in accordance with Article 23 of the revised regulations for overseas Chinese primary and secondary schools. (Article 2) The board of directors of overseas Chinese primary and secondary schools is the representative of the school's establishment. (Article 3) The board of directors of overseas Chinese primary and secondary schools shall legally include the school's name, such as the Board of Directors of XX Middle School or Primary School. If there are special circumstances for setting another name, it shall be clearly stated when applying for registration. (Article 4) Any Chinese citizen who meets the following qualifications may be elected as a director of the board of directors of overseas Chinese primary and secondary schools: (1) Those who established the school; (2) Those who have donated funds to the school; (3) Local education experts and those who are enthusiastic about promoting education; (4) Staff members of local education organizations. (Article 5) The board of directors of overseas Chinese primary and secondary schools shall set up the following staff members: (1) Chairman (1 person); (2) Vice-Chairman (1 to 3 persons); (3) Finance (2 persons); (4) Auditor (2 persons); (5) Accountant (1 person); (6) Clerk (1 person). (Supplementary Item 1) The method and term of election of directors shall be determined by the board of directors themselves. (Supplementary Item 2) If there are too many directors, a standing committee of 5 to 9 directors may be established. (Supplementary Item 3) If there are standing committee directors, the above-mentioned staff members shall be concurrently held by the standing committee directors. (Article 6) The functions and powers of the board of directors of overseas Chinese primary and secondary schools are stipulated as follows: (1) Fundraising and safekeeping of funds; (2) Purchasing and safekeeping of school property; (3) Planning annual expenses and temporary expenses such as construction equipment; (4) Selecting and reappointing the principal; (5) Reviewing the budget and final accounts; (6) Handling school registration matters; (7) Representing the school in handling matters with the local government. (Article 7) The principal selected by the board of directors shall be responsible for the school's administration. The directors of the board of directors may inspect the school at any time, and when there is a suggestion for the development of school affairs, it shall be submitted to the board of directors for deliberation and resolution, and the principal shall handle it as appropriate. (Article 8) The board of directors meeting of overseas Chinese primary and secondary schools shall be chaired by the chairman. When the chairman is absent, the vice-chairman shall be the chairman. (Article 9) The staff members of the board of directors of overseas Chinese primary and secondary schools shall not concurrently serve as teachers or staff members of the school. (Article 10) When the board of directors of overseas Chinese primary and secondary schools applies for registration of the school, it shall fill in the detailed information in accordance with the "Overview" section of the overseas Chinese school registration form and submit it to the competent consulate for forwarding to the Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission and the Ministry of Education for joint registration. (Article 11) When the board of directors of overseas Chinese primary and secondary schools is reorganized, the reorganization shall be reported to the competent consulate for verification and forwarding to the Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission and the Ministry of Education for record. (Article 12) When an overseas Chinese primary and secondary school is dissolved due to an incident, its board of directors shall report the situation to the competent consulate for forwarding to the Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission and the Ministry of Education for record within one week. (Article 13) If there are special circumstances in which an overseas Chinese primary and secondary school cannot establish a board of directors, the school founder may apply to the Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission and the Ministry of Education for approval to waive the functions and powers of the board of directors, which shall be exercised by the founder. (Article 14) These regulations shall be jointly promulgated and implemented by the Ministry of Education and the Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission.

Ministry of Education to Promote Civil Education; Provinces Will Be Divided into Guidance Areas 244

Each area director will be responsible

And will be required to reduce illiteracy

In order to promote public education and improve national knowledge, the Ministry of Education has drafted a plan to promote national public education. This plan has been completed and will be implemented as soon as Minister Wang Jiawei reviews it. According to sources in the local education community, the steps for implementing this plan will first involve dividing each province and city into several public education guidance areas and selecting reputable individuals as area directors to be responsible for overseeing public education in each area. After the establishment of the guidance areas, deadlines will be set for reducing illiteracy so that the livelihoods of the people will not continue to decline.

Yuan TongLi Departs for the East This Morning 245

Transfers to Europe and the United States to study culture, books, etc.

Photocopies of ancient calligraphy and paintings are brought for display

(Beijing, 22nd) Yuan TongLi went to Tianjin at 4 pm on the 22nd and is scheduled to take the Japanese ship "Zenko" to Kobe on the morning of the 23rd, where he will stay briefly before heading to the United States and Europe to study culture. Around May, he plans to visit various construction projects in the Soviet Union on his way back to China. According to Yuan, this trip to Europe and the United States will involve a detailed study of cultural books and other book-related industries. At the same time, he will introduce Chinese culture and national treasures to Western countries. Photocopies of ancient calligraphy and paintings from the Song, Yuan, and Ming dynasties preserved in the Forbidden City have been packed into two boxes for display and will be selected for distribution to friendly nations.

Huang BingKun Discusses the General Situation of Overseas Chinese Education in Southeast Asia 252

A reporter met with Mr. Huang Bingkun, who recently returned from Southeast Asia, at his residence yesterday. Mr. Huang has been teaching in overseas Chinese schools in various parts of Southeast Asia for more than ten years. This time, he brought his family back to his hometown in retirement. He has a good understanding of the situation of overseas Chinese education in Southeast Asia. The details of what Mr. Huang told are as follows: Mr. Huang said that there are many overseas Chinese in Southeast Asia, especially people from Guangdong and Fujian. In addition to the foreign governments widely establishing schools to accommodate overseas Chinese in order to colonize them, many overseas Chinese who are enthusiastic about education also set up schools themselves. Especially in British and Dutch colonies, there are many overseas Chinese schools. There are already more than two hundred schools in Singapore. All

School Administration　Except for overseas Chinese schools in Siam, which are subject to the constraints of the independent country's education system, other overseas Chinese schools in British, Dutch, and French colonies are independent. The highest administrative body is the board of directors. Most of the school sites are located in the ancestral halls. Guangdong, such as Guangzhao, Chaozhou, Rongshu, and Hainan ancestral halls, and Fujian, such as Zhangzhou, Tongan, and Anxi ancestral halls, have very few buildings. Most of the school directors are businessmen who do not understand education and are too busy with business to care about it. Therefore, they only have a nominal title. Sometimes, conflicts arise due to unclear authority, interfering with teaching affairs, and affecting political school affairs. Although the ancestral government once ordered the consulates in Southeast Asia to concurrently manage

Overseas Chinese Education, but the consuls generally regard it as a mere formality. Secondly, overseas Chinese schools are sometimes subject to interference from the government where they reside. For example, the British government promulgated the Overseas Chinese School Registration Ordinance and set up a Chinese inspector. The Siamese government interferes even more severely. All Chinese who serve as principals and teachers must pass the Siamese government's examination. Those who do not understand Siamese are not allowed to be employed. Therefore, the curriculum of each school devotes up to twenty hours per week to Siamese. As for the funding of each school, it used to be more than sufficient. In recent years, affected by the global economic panic, the commercial situation in Southeast Asia has been very sluggish, and funding has gradually become difficult. Moreover, each school has no standard for the distribution of funds, and the budget is also very chaotic, which is not seen in domestic schools.

The Teachers of Each School　Very few are introduced from the country. Most of them are hired through advertisements and value diplomas, regardless of experience and knowledge. The most important thing is Mandarin and calligraphy. If they can speak fluent plain Mandarin, the students will respect them. There is no fixed standard for the curriculum. Generally, more attention is paid to singing and dancing and English. Most of the English teachers are Siamese, and the Chinese teachers are all in charge of one grade. They must teach all subjects, whether it is books or singing. However, the treatment is also becoming increasingly harsh.

Overseas Chinese Students　Have a patriotic ideology and are happy to listen to explanations of current events in the motherland. However, growing up in the tropics, they are full of energy and often fight in the classroom, are addicted to gambling, and like to eat snacks. Students are not fixed in the schools they attend. The reason is that most of their families are engaged in business and are sometimes rich and sometimes poor, moving from east to west. Therefore, students are registered in the school every week. This is the most difficult thing to handle. In short, overseas Chinese education is currently in a very chaotic state. I hope the government authorities will send personnel to inspect and improve it.

Soochow Law School Classes Began Yesterday 255

Registration for students at Soochow University Law School in the local area has continued this semester and has been completed. Classes officially began yesterday. Spring and Autumn

Rose with Thorns 258

— Yongzi

The most taboo thing in the life of a couple is a horizontal shape, because although the horizontal couple life is very harmonious on the surface, and the neighbors don't hear the sound of scolding, the interest in life is definitely not as good as the wavy shape. Therefore, a certain scholar, not my friend, once advocated the theory that "couples should often quarrel, and even fight." His argument is that couples should often quarrel over small things that don't need to be argued about, and they should also quarrel and even fight. After such a big fight, the couple reconciled, and the interest in life at that time was more delicious than before the fight. After that, after a certain period of time, the love between the couple gradually faded, then they had to find another opportunity to play again. This is the so-called wavy couple life, which is the only good way to keep the love between the couple young.

Because of the principle of wavy couple life, I understood the principle of rose with thorns that is supported by people. People's lives are naturally too monotonous and boring. Rich people roll around in their thighs, roll around in wine glasses, and roll around in money eyes. After getting tired of rolling around, they shouted that they would go back to the countryside, or take a walk on the road alone, or live a civilian life for one or two days, and they would feel very comfortable. On the contrary, if a poor boy rolls around in disease, rolls around in life, and rolls around in all the terrors of the times, and can't catch his breath, he will also temporarily forget all the pain and pursue a moment of pleasure to adjust his spirit. Therefore, when miners work in the dark and gloomy underground, they will also hum and compose music, and the dock workers standing under the crane that is enough to destroy their own lives will have to glance at the fully curvy female customers, meditating on everything, and smiling mysteriously. Therefore, most people do not love roses because roses have thorns and are afraid of being stabbed.

People in this society are demanding a large number of roses with thorns, and they need all kinds of wavy lives, 丨丨naturally, not just couple lives, otherwise, everyone will feel monotonous and lonely, and they will curse the emptiness of life even more.

Wu Ziyu Enjoys Spring Lanterns 259

— Zheng YiMei

General Xing PengLai Wu Ziyu has been living in seclusion in Youyan recently, hiding his whereabouts. People have forgotten his spirit of leading hundreds of thousands of soldiers and drinking horses on the Great Wall. But he is also tired of talking about military affairs, and spends all day writing bamboo and plum blossoms as the only pastime. He opens the window to draw bamboo branches, and the big wind presses the bamboo to worship the plum blossoms. The brokers are deeply interested. It is really rare among today's warriors.

The end of winter and the return of spring, the scenery and customs follow the old, hanging lanterns and banners to decorate the New Year. Wu suddenly had a clear interest, and specially ordered more than 300 various lanterns from the lantern painting shop on the first street of Langfang, all of which were made of thin yarn. Wu has always admired Guan Yu and Yue Fei as people, and specially hired a painter to paint stories such as Romance of the Three Kingdoms and The Legend of Yue on the lantern yarn. Adding colorful colors made it even more brilliant. Guan Yue was even more vividly painted, with a kind of Confucian general demeanor. Once night fell, the lanterns were lit with candles, illuminating the Lantern Festival, as bright as the morning sun. Wu invited many old subordinates and set up a banquet to watch them. The lamplight reflected, and everyone's faces were red. Wu couldn't help but chant the poems of his predecessors: The fiery tree comes out when the feast is held, and the lamp screen surrounds the seat diagonally. He floated three whites in a row. The subordinates knew that the host's interest was soaring, so they flew a note to summon several famous singers to sing a few songs. The pink, white, and black, the jade smile and the pearl frown, under the lamplight, became even more graceful and beautiful. Although Wu belonged to the male Liu Hui from Lu, he did not understand lust on weekdays, but at this time, he couldn't help but feel short of breath and long on affection. After listening to the melodious Wu Ou, he praised it greatly, saying: No wonder the world has the proverb of being born in Suzhou and living in Hangzhou. I deeply regret that I don't have the blessing to visit Suzhou and Hangzhou to see the beautiful scenery of the lake and mountains. As he spoke, he drank one cup after another. After the banquet, the guests dispersed, Wu was already so drunk that he could not walk, and was helped into bed by his attendants. The next day, he wrote a poem to record the event, and asked his subordinates to harmonize the chapters. I heard that there were many good poems, but unfortunately I couldn't copy them, otherwise writing them here would also be good material.

Three Kinds of Water Heaters Invented by Design 260

— Rong

The Hangzhou factory of Sanyou Industrial Company has always used steam heating for dyeing water, which is the same as other dyeing factories. Last year, because Tian Xuwo Sheng went to visit, he said that he had invented a kind of water mouse in the past, which was very clever and could save a lot of time. Therefore, Mr. Chen Wanyun asked him to try to make one for comparison. As a result, 60 pounds of cold water with the same volume can be heated to 80 degrees Celsius in 7 minutes, while the original disc coil can only be heated to 60 degrees, saving time by more than one-third, which is enough to increase work and efficiency by more than 37%. Therefore, he entrusted the Home Industry Cooperative to specially make 38 pieces, which have been completely refitted. According to the description, the reason for the invention is that when ordinary steam is heated, many bubbles float on the water surface, resulting in heat loss, and the ones that escape from the water surface account for more than three-tenths, which can be said to be a waste. Therefore, this device is made by using the principle of vacuum spray. Its shape is like a water mouse in a firecracker, so it is named water mouse. It makes the steam enter from the back and absorb the cold water from the tail end, and spray out from the head end, so that the water rotates and circulates continuously. There are absolutely no bubbles floating on the water surface, so it is very easy to heat. Each cubic foot of cold water is heated to 60 degrees Celsius, no more than three minutes in summer and no more than five minutes in winter. This is just a method, and the materials are very cheap, only five yuan per piece. There is also a "hand-shaped heater", the principle is the same, but its uses are different, because the water mouse can only be used in the water storage tank, while the hand-shaped heater can draw water from the well and transport it to the application site, turning it into hot water continuously. The suction force can reach 20 feet, the blowing force can reach 15 feet, and the horizontal flow can be transported regardless of distance. It can also be branched into two lines in the middle, and the water comes out very quickly. The cost of materials per piece is 25 yuan. If water is taken from the water tower, there is another kind, called "Guo Shanlong", the principle is the same as the water mouse, but a water pipe is connected to the head end, which can transport horizontal flow and branch it to send it far away. It can also adjust the water intake, so that the high temperature can reach 90 degrees Celsius, or reduce the temperature to 30 degrees Celsius to meet the purpose of use. The cost of each piece is only 15 yuan. All three kinds of heaters can be said to be fast and clever, increasing work efficiency a lot. However, the angle is very important when making them. A slight deviation will prevent the water from being sprayed into a mist, which will consume a lot of steam power and damage the coal fire. Therefore, each device must be measured by the inventor himself and pointed out with ink before drilling the hole.

Green Apples and Oranges 261

— Huai Qu

In recent months, what I have feared seeing most is apples, especially green apples.

Whenever I walked past the door of a fruit store, I would always lower my head or look elsewhere. If I accidentally wasn't careful, and my gaze came into contact with those glossy green apples, they could give me an extremely harsh stimulation.

In the past, among fruits, my favorite to eat was apples. I also loved its glossy green color, which contained the beauty of a maiden. Since getting to know her, her preferences influenced me, making me love green apples even more.

When she was around, what she loved to look at most was everything green, especially that apple-like light green. Her clothing when she was at school was almost inseparable from this green color, year-round. If she happened to buy a few new books, she would also use green paper to wrap the covers.

Not only for apples did she love the green, but also for other fruits, she often didn't mind that they were unripe, and liked to choose the green ones.

I remember during last year's winter vacation, we were both preparing to return to our hometowns. On the Sunday of the week before the vacation, I, along with her brother Dongwei, accompanied her to buy snacks. Dongwei went to the food shop to buy oranges, and she only picked out the green ones.

"What is this?" Dongwei asked in this way.

"I feel very sorry for it! I love its color very much! Alas! This is its innocent color. It doesn't use bright red to entice us, it has no intention of contributing to the outside world! You wicked people, why do you have to pick it off so forcefully!"

She said to her brother with a smile.

Her smile was a smile containing lament!

Afterwards, I jokingly said to her:

"Green oranges, really have no intention of contributing to people? Maybe the time hasn't come yet?"

She lowered her head in thought, and never explained this question to me.

Fourth Company Commander of the Northeast 262

— Zhang Henshui

Chapter Twenty-Four

Sharing Wine and Food, Reveling and Bidding Farewell with Tears

Burning the Midnight Oil, Whispering Dreams and Passing the Long Night

Ziqiang slammed the table and said: "So it turns out you have such a great skill, why didn't you say so earlier? Otherwise, these past few days, I would have asked you to sing every day." Guizhi smiled and said: "Do you think I am a theater fanatic? Today is a special situation, that's why I shamelessly started singing." Ziqiang said: "What's so special about today?" Guizhi said: "It's just a farewell dinner for you." Ziqiang smiled and said: "Now I know that when a husband is about to leave home, he can receive special favor from his wife. In the future, I should always leave home." Upon hearing this, the color on Guizhi's face couldn't help but change a little. Ziqiang then explained with a smile: "What I mean by always leaving home is coming back three times a month, so I'll only be leaving home three times a month. Can you also give me a farewell dinner like today?" Guizhi smiled and said: "Just for you to drink two taels of wine and listen to me sing a few lines off-key, it's not worth it, right?" Ziqiang said, "In this world, what's worth it and what's not worth it? It all depends on each person's own assessment. A small diamond, at most, can be worth tens of thousands. May I ask, what's the use of that? As for me, I love to eat roasted sweet potatoes the most. They're sweet, fragrant, and hot, but they only cost a few copper coins, and a person can eat their fill. People in the world don't think much of it, so it can't become anything great. So to speak, good and bad aren't fixed, it all depends on whether people like it or not. I think two taels of wine and a short song are worth me running around a long distance." Guizhi smiled and said: "You're right, I'll sing another short song for you to listen to, to thank you for considering me a confidante." Ziqiang held his cup, tilted his head, and listened outside again, then asked: "What time is it? It sounds like the fourth watch." Guizhi said: "You don't have to worry about that at all. Tonight, we'll just eat a little, drink a little, and have a little fun." (319)

Miscellaneous Remarks

Patriots Never Forget the Sky 263

— Nanhai Shaou

Using Statistics to Prove the Safety of Aviation

"Riding the wind, how light and ethereal!" I often recall Lie Yukou's fluttering fantasy of ascending to immortality; it's just a pity that I never learned aviation since I was young.

Although the slogan "Aviation to Save the Nation" has been almost sung to the high heavens, in reality, our "Air Force" has not yet left the "national borders" 丨丨our airspace丨丨. Our aviation technicians are very backward in terms of quantity and technology.

"The son of a thousand pieces of gold does not sit under an overhanging eave." "A gentleman does not stand under a crumbling wall,"…These are all intoxicating drugs that cultivate our "fear of death inferiority complex." In the future, we must create a few new slogans, new creeds, such as:

Patriots never forget the "sky"!

Warriors never forget "broken arms"!

Having creeds and slogans alone is not enough to encourage true courage. We must use some method to encourage the general youth's interest in aviation, so that everyone develops a lasting frenzy. Then, using the old phrases to encourage reading, we can hum:

In the "sky" there is a beautiful woman! In the "sky" there is a fast Cloud Pavilion! But this is too ridiculous.

Only by breaking the inferiority complex of "fear of death" can we generate an interest in adventure; so I found some ironclad factual statistics to explain that aviation is safe and not dangerous.

According to Australian aviation statistics, in the past five years,

Aviation route 9,901,431 miles

Number of passengers carried 250,582

Number of deaths in accidents 32

Number of injuries in accidents 21

On average, one person dies in an accident every 225,000 miles of flight, and one person is injured every 210,000 miles.

In 1930, public aviation flew 598,000 miles, carrying 7,835 passengers, without any accidents. Regular aviation flew 759,000 miles, carrying 8,096 passengers, with one accident, killing one pilot and injuring one bystander.

According to statistics at the end of last year,

In the United States, on average, one person dies in an accident every 900,000 miles of flight. In the United Kingdom, one person dies every 100,000 miles. In France, one person dies every 1,490,000 miles.

This slight danger is really nothing compared to tigers hurting people in the city.

Airplanes are much safer than cars.

According to the 1930 British car (motorcycle) injury statistics:

Number of accidents 156,793

Number of deaths 7,305

Number of injuries 177,895

Looking at it this way, flying by plane is much safer than riding in a car. Why do ordinary people always see riding in a car as a mundane thing, and flying in a plane as an adventurous thing?

The driving of motorcycles, in addition to the problems that may occur with the vehicle itself, has many obstacles on the road, and dangers can occur at any time, so the tragic accidents of car crashes are commonplace. As for airplanes, there are no utility poles or trees in the sky, nor are there people. Rising and falling, moving forward, backward, left, right, up, and down, can all be done freely. In addition to the occasional problems that occur with the vehicle itself and the changes in the weather, it can be said that there are no other obstacles. Based on the usual assumptions, it is much safer.

Number of passenger planes in various countries in recent years

Therefore, civil aviation in various countries is rapidly seeking to compete with ships and trains for seats.

Country Number of planes Number of passengers Note

UK...34...45,150...Full year 1932

France...259...26,893...Same as above

Italy...82...43,300...Same as above

Germany...178...98,489...Same as above

Netherlands...43...21,020...Same as above

United States...544...248,954...First half of 1933

Looking at these facts and clear numbers, it can be proven that "Is aviation dangerous? It is not dangerous!" Here, I respectfully wish "the nation that fears death" everyone "a stubborn man has integrity! A cowardly man has ambition!"

Various remittance funds amounted to more than 300,000, and more than 20,000 in cash was collected. Securities

The Last Day of February: Bond Market Squeezes Shorts, Sharp Tax 269

Except for Disarmament, All Show New High Prices

Yesterday, the Chinese Securities Exchange was the last day of February futures. Although the market had many shorts and longs vying for position, the short squeeze was ultimately the most severe. Except for the fact that the price of disarmament slightly loosened due to the squeezing relationship, the rest continued to reach new high prices. Sentiment was strong, and there were too many shorts, and they were already at the end of their rope. Because there were no goods to deliver, they had no choice but to painfully cut losses or roll over. The disarmament category was known to be difficult to short, so the longs were crowded. Those without real strength had no choice but to roll over at the market price. As a result, all categories were good, except for disarmament, which was weak. When the market opened in the morning, there were a lot of small short coverings and short rollovers. Number 50 bought quite a bit. Market prices rose uniformly by 1 or 2 jiao to about half a yuan. Disarmament was slightly weak due to long rollovers, down by 1 or 2 jiao. At the close, Numbers 11 and 16 sold or rolled over quite a bit, while Numbers 5, 26, and 50 were still needed. Scattered retail investors were still enthusiastically buying. Market prices mostly continued to increase by 2 or 3 jiao. Among them, the consolidated disarmament was slightly better. In the end, except for disarmament, which was slightly lower by 3 jiao and 5 fen, the rest continued to increase by 1 or 2 jiao to 6 or 7 jiao. Today is only doing one month of March futures, and the market has not yet shown any loopholes. The total transaction volume was 17,871,000 yuan, including 11,000 yuan in spot goods, 5,380,000 in unified salt tax futures, 1,715,000 in disarmament stores, 1,535,000 in 19 customs duties, 3,190,000 in 20 coils and 20 customs duties, 3,465,000 in short gold six, 2,060,000 in long gold nine six, and 620,000 in 18 customs duties and consolidated disbursements. No Possibility of Resolving the Standard Yarn Reform Issue 272

Shareholder Group Primarily Wants to Replace Brokers, Facing Opposition

The Shanghai Yarn and Cloth Exchange has been arguing about the standard reform issue for a long time, and it has not been resolved. Both sides have gone to extremes. Yesterday, the brokers' side convened a general meeting to discuss everything. As a result, the majority still agreed to use Ren Zhong yarn as the standard. However, according to market rumors, the shareholder group is doing its utmost to advocate for changing to Golden Rooster yarn as the standard, preparing to list and open trading on March 1, with simultaneous operations for the May, June, July, August, and April contract months. However, according to news from the brokers' side, if new standard yarn is used, they intend to refuse all transactions as a form of resistance. What will actually happen remains to be seen.

Grains

Factories Are Dumping Large Quantities of Futures Flour 275

Borrowing Wheat Until 4 Yuan 1 Jiao

After the flour market opened last year, prices for all contract months fell across the board. Quotations for foreign wheat fluctuated very little, with a difference of about 4 fen. Therefore, the market was initially stable. However, major factories, such as Fuxin and Fufeng, continued to release supplies, and distant contract months were constantly being offered. It was rumored that the government was borrowing wheat at 4 yuan and 1 jiao, but no one accepted it. It is estimated that the factories would only consider 4 yuan and 5 fen, or perhaps have an intention to import. However, Fuxin had already contracted for a ship of Argentine wheat at a price of only 4 yuan and 1.5 jiao. As a result, the market was dominated by selling pressure, with trading volume reaching over 400,000 bags, of which factory holdings accounted for about 200,000 bags. With the steady decline in foreign wheat prices, customer sales remained limited. Further declines are likely in the future. The current month is still one jiao away, but months after March have all fallen below the one jiao threshold. As a result, the current month fell by 2.5 fen compared to the previous day, March and April fell by 2.75 fen, May fell by 2 fen, and June and July fell by 2.5 fen.

Small Factories Tend to Purchase Wheat for the Current Month 276

After the wheat market opened in the morning and afternoon, prices for all contract months showed a slow and steady decline. Quotations for foreign wheat fluctuated very little. Although the current month is close to delivery, and the prices of foreign wheat continue to decline, in theory, there should be few positive factors. However, it is rumored that small factories are quite interested in purchasing the current month's standard. Therefore, although trading volume is small, the market is supported. Trading in distant contract months is also not very active. However, with continued transactions of current foreign wheat, although the decline is small, the market sentiment is generally weak. As a result, the current month rebounded by 4 fen, March by a small 2 fen, and April by a small 2 fen. July had already crossed the 3 yuan threshold and fell to 2 yuan and 9.5 jiao, a drop of 5 fen. The current wheat market has little trading, and prices are trending flat and soft. The opening price for Bengbu wheat is 3 yuan, 3 jiao, and 4 fen, and the price for Yaowan wheat is 3 yuan, 3 jiao, and 9 fen, with an estimated 500 bags purchased by Fuxin.

Cargoes on the Way Arriving, Owners Seeking to Unload, Hunan Red Brown Rice Suddenly Drops 2 Jiao 277

Yesterday, the Hokkien group was still actively purchasing Xiangxian rice. Local shops continued to inquire, and just as sentiment was turning positive, cargo owners suddenly devalued their prices in an attempt to unload. Furthermore, all cargo owners wanted to clear their inventory. Because current inventories are very large, in addition to the new arrivals at the end of last winter, cargoes loaded during the New Year can arrive within days. Due to the above-mentioned reasons, the market was oversupplied. After the market opened, prices for all grades of Xiangxian rice fell across the board, especially for Hunan red brown rice, which had a large inventory. The price suddenly dropped by 2 jiao. Other mid-grade and lower grades of rice also fell by a small amount of jiao. High-grade rice also fell by a small 5 fen. Hunan red brown rice opened at 5 yuan, 6 jiao, and 7 fen, with an estimated 2,500 bags purchased by the Hokkien group. Also, 150 bags of cleaned rice were purchased at 6 yuan. Jiangxi late-season milled rice sold 373 bags at 7 yuan, 6 jiao, and 2 to 4 fen. Beijing brown rice sold 175 bags at 5 yuan and 6 jiao. Quanzhou Nanjing milled Xian rice sold 2,000 bags at 6 yuan, 5 jiao, and 4 to 5 fen. Guangzhou milled red rice sold 100 bags at 6 yuan and 8.5 jiao. Local shops purchased 700 bags of Hunan milled oil rice at 7 yuan, 2 jiao, and 3 fen, and 200 bags of milled rice at 6 yuan and 5 jiao. Jiangxi early-season milled rice sold 48 bags at 5 yuan and 9 jiao. No other transactions were reported.

River Rice Stagnant in Sales, Price Drops 278

(Shanghai South) Yesterday, the supply from various groups was particularly scarce, with only about a dozen arrivals. The Hokkien group's appetite was also weak, with a total of 700 to 800 bags brought in by the Northern and Southern Oceans groups. Local shops also have fewer storage, so the market is showing a soft trend. Prices for Jiangsu and Zhejiang groups' Nangang and other japonica rice, as well as Qinghong Songjiang late rice, have all fallen by 2 to 3 fen. Changzhou japonica rice is out of stock. Du Yangjian and various other grades are either lacking in stock or have few sales, leaving the market unsettled.

(Shanghai North) Yesterday, 15 or 16 boats of river rice arrived. Sales by various groups in the market were very sluggish. Prices for japonica rice, thin rice, and early rice have fallen by a small amount of jiao. Prices for Yangjian and Dujian have been reduced by several fen. Prices for Baiyuan and Yinyuan are stable. Kejian is flat and weak.

Oil Market: The Pre- and Post-Spring Market Conditions for Tung Oil 279

The tung oil and beeswax industry is a small one. The largest firms only have annual sales of 500,000 to 600,000, while ordinary firms only have 200,000 to 300,000. The entire market only has seven or eight firms. Three or four firms consider tung oil as their main business and beeswax as their secondary business, while another three or four firms consider beeswax as their main business and tung oil as their secondary business. Although they belong to the same industry, their focus is slightly different. The main use of tung oil is for candle making, with soap making as a secondary use. However, in recent years, the amount used in soap making has increased significantly, almost surpassing the amount used in candle making. Furthermore, soap factories trade in whole numbers, while candle sales are in smaller amounts. Therefore, soap factory transactions can stimulate a price increase, which is always noticed by the general public. However, soap making does not necessarily require tung oil. Butter, coconut oil, and other oils can also be used, so one can choose the cheaper option. Candle making, on the other hand, requires tung oil. Last year, because butter and coconut oil were cheaper than tung oil, the market for tung oil inevitably declined, and local firms did not have as much business as in previous years. Beeswax relies entirely on customer sales, with candle merchants being secondary. In the past, sales to Guangdong were the largest, but they have also declined recently. Other groups in Shandong and Yantai are very small, so beeswax sales have also gradually declined. Although both tung oil and beeswax are necessary for candle making, the sales of candle shops are no longer comparable to those in previous years. Therefore, firms' business is inevitably affected. It is also heard that customer accounts overdue for the new year are quite numerous. Making a profit is not easy. The various firms have a solid foundation, so profits and losses can be adjusted. Even if a profit is announced, it is unlikely to be the actual result for the year. If you ask about the actual profit or loss, those who are engaged in this business may not be able to give a definite answer, let alone a superficial investigation by a reporter. The market conditions, inventory, and estimated spring prices at the time of the year-end closing are roughly reported below. The closing price in Hankou was 17 yuan, 1 jiao, and 2 fen per stone for heavy Jing, 16 yuan, 7 jiao, and 8 fen for branch heavy, 16 yuan, 4 jiao, and 5 fen for flat Jing, 17 yuan per dan for Chashe oil, 16 yuan, 3 jiao, and 4 fen for Front Row Jianma, and 15 yuan, 7 jiao, and 8 fen for Tianjin oil. The spring market has not yet opened, but it is predicted that 6 to 7 jiao can be added. The inventory of heavy Jing, flat Jing, Branch Jiang, Tianjin, Chashe, and others are each about 1,000 to 2,000 pieces. There are about 4,000 to 5,000 pieces of Macheng oil. Because the water level in the upper reaches of the Yangtze River is low in winter, the supply is weak, and the inventory is also thin. When the spring water rises, the arrivals will definitely surge, and the market will definitely change at that time. The closing price in this port was 20 yuan and 8 jiao per stone for heavy Jing, 20 yuan for flat Jing, 19 yuan, 4 jiao, and 6 fen for Tianjin, and 18 yuan, 2 jiao, and 3 fen per dan (local scale) for Macheng oil. The opening spring price is 21 yuan and 8 jiao per stone for heavy Jing, 20 yuan for flat Jing, 19 yuan and 4 jiao per dan for Chashe, and 19 yuan for Macheng, an increase of about 1 yuan compared to the closing price. The total inventory in the market is about 2,000 to 3,000 pieces. After the closing of accounts, about 1,000 pieces were borrowed and loaded from Hankou. The customer goods were all sold out at the end of the year and need to be awaited. Furthermore, news from Kuozhou is that the spring market opened at 15 yuan and 6 jiao per stone for Tilan, 21 yuan for Neiping, and 12 yuan and 4 jiao for Xiaoxi. Jiaxing local truck oil is 20 yuan per dan (local scale), which has also increased slightly.

Piece Goods: Great Progress in the Wool Fabric Market 280

Recently, the wool fabric market has made great progress. After the market opened, prices were firmer than in previous years, and sales of various goods were wide. Although arrivals were crowded and Japanese goods were abundant, the trend is still active. Currently, in addition to plaid gabardine and plain serge, a large amount of general woolen fabrics have been offered. Especially, the sales price of green tribute cloth and woolen herringbone overcoat cloth are selling well. Therefore, traders are optimistic, predicting that customers will start buying soon and that sales of spring goods will start, and that the market will make even more progress.

Hardware: Tinplate Sees Good Conditions in Both China and Abroad 281

Local Situation: In recent days, factories have completed dozens of transactions, offering over 1,000 boxes. Customer group interest has also been good, and the market conditions are unusually buoyant. Berlin Telegram Also Raised Prices: Yesterday's telegram reported 34 shillings for 90-pound double-linked, an increase of 3 shillings, and 36 shillings for 100-pound, also an increase of 2 shillings. Colleagues have not made any transactions.

Silk and Tea: Overseas Silk Sales Turn Weak 282
